Ruling on Imam Standing in the Mihrab
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of the imam standing in the mihrab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two Hanafi opinions regarding the imam standing in the mihrab and identify the mufta bihi ruling with its condition of necessity.

Core Idea
The imam's standing in the mihrab is makruh tahrimi, but necessity due to crowding overrides the dislike.

You have likely seen imams leading prayer from the mihrab. Is this practice always acceptable? Within the Hanafi school, there is a detailed discussion about its ruling. This lesson unpacks the reasons behind the dislike and the conditions that permit it, helping you understand how legal reasoning operates within a single madhhab.

Guided Path
1
State the base ruling
Identify that Muhammad al-Shaybani declared it makruh in al-Jami' al-Saghir without specifying the reason. This sets the foundation for the dispute.
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah, so it carries weight.
2
Examine the two causes
List the two reasons given by the mashayikh: (1) the imam becomes distinct in place, resembling the People of the Book; (2) the congregation may be confused about the imam's state.
These lead to different rulings.
3
Trace the two opinions
According to the first cause, the dislike is absolute; according to the second, it is conditional on confusion arising.
This is the core ikhtilaf.
4
Analyze the counter-argument
Consider the argument from Fath al-Qadir: the imam's distinction is legally required, so the mihrab is just a marker and not disliked.
This is a minority Hanafi view.
5
Conclude with tarjih and exception
The author prefers the absolute dislike view, but notes permission in necessity (crowding), citing al-Walwaji.
This is the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وقيام الإمام لا سجوده في الطاق) أي المحراب لأن قيامه فيه يشبه صنيع أهل الكتاب بخلاف سجوده فيه وقيامه خارجه. هكذا علل به في الهداية وهو أحد الطريقين للمشايخ، وأصله أن محمداً صرح بالكراهة في الجامع الصغير ولم يفصل، فاختلف المشايخ في سببها فقيل كونه يصير ممتازاً عنهم في المكان لأنه في معنى بيت آخر وذلك صنيع أهل الكتاب. واقتصر عليه في الهداية واختاره الإمام السرخسي وقال : إنه الأوجه . وقيل : اشتباه حاله على من على يمينه ويساره، فعلى الطريقة الأولى يكره مطلقاً، وعلى الثانية لا يكره عند عدم الاشتباه . وفي فتح القدير : ولا يخفي أن امتياز الإمام مقرر مطلوب في الشرع في حق المكان حتى كان التقدم واجباً عليه وغاية ما هنا كونه في خصوص مكان ولا أثر لذلك لأنه يحاذي وسط الصف وهو المطلوب إذ قيامه في غير محاذاته مكروه وغايته اتفاق الملتين في بعض الأحكام، ولا بدع فيه على أن أهل الكتاب إنما يخصون الإمام بالمكان المرتفع على ما قيل فلا تشبه .اهـ. وقد يقال إن امتياز الإمام المطلوب في الشرع حاصل بتقدمه من غير أن يقف في مكان آخر، فمتى أمكن تمييزه من غير تشبه بأهل الكتاب تعين، فحينئذ وقوفه في المحراب تشبه بأهل الكتاب لغير حاجة فكره مطلقاً ولهذا قال الولوالجي في فتاواه وصاحب التجنيس : إذا ضاق المسجد بمن خلف الإمام على القوم لا بأس بأن يقوم الإمام في الطاق لأنه تعذر الأمر عليه، وإن لم يضق المسجد بمن خلف الإمام لا ينبغي للإمام أن يقوم في الطاق لأنه يشبه تباين المكانين .اهـ. يعني وحقيقة اختلاف المكان تمنع الجواز فشبهة الاختلاف توجب الكراهة وهو وإن كان المحراب من المسجد كما العادة المستمرة فصورته وهيئته اقتضت شبهة الاختلاف فالحاصل أن مقتضى ظاهر الرواية كراهة قيامه في المحراب مطلقاً، سواء اشتبه حال الإمام أو لا، وسواء كان المحراب من المسجد أم لا . وإنما لم يكره سجوده في المحراب إذا كان قدماه خارجه لأن العبرة للقدم في مكان الصلاة حتى تشترط طهارته رواية واحدة بخلاف مكان السجود إذ فيه روايتان. وكذا لو حلف لا يدخل دار فلان يحنث بوضع القدمين وإن كان باقي بدنه خارجها، والصيد إذا كان رجلاه في الحرم ورأسه خارج منه فهو صيد الحرم ففيه الجزاء.
قوله : (وقد يقال الخ ذكر نحوه الشيخ إبراهيم الحلبي في شرحه على المنية لكن جنح ابن أمير حاج الحلبي في شرحه على المنية إلى تأييد ما في فتح القدير حيث قال: قلت ويؤيده ما قدمناه عن قاضيخان أن التشبه بأهل الكتاب لا يكره في كل شيء الخ. وليس هذا من المذموم في شيء وكونه يشبه اختلاف المكانين وحقيقة الاختلاف تمنع الجواز فشبهة الاختلاف توجب الكراهة يعارض بما لو تقدم في بعض بقاع المسجد على القوم من غير أن يدخل المحراب ولا قائل بالكراهة فيه فكذا هنا اهـ . قلت : يجاب عن المعارضة المذكورة بما أشار إليه المؤلف من أن المحراب وإن كان من لكن صورته وهيئته تقتضي شبهة اختلاف المكان لأنه ليس كبقيه بقاع المسجد من حيث إنه يصلي فيه بخصوصه كل أحد، وإنما جعل علامة لمكان وقوف الإمام وأن يكون سجوده فيه لا قيامه لأنه لم يبن لأن يقوم الإمام في داخله ولا لأن يصلي فيه الناس وإنما هو علامة كما قلنا فأشبه خارج المسجد فصار بمنزلة مكان آخر بخلاف بقية بقاع المسجد تأمل
His saying: (and the imam's standing, not his prostration, in the arch) i.e., the mihrab, because his standing in it resembles the practice of the People of the Book, contrary to his prostration in it and his standing outside it. Thus it is explained in al-Hidayah, and it is one of two ways of the mashayikh. Its origin is that Muhammad explicitly stated dislike in al-Jami' al-Saghir without specifying the reason, so the mashayikh differed on its cause. One view: it makes him distinguished from them in place, as if in another house, and that is the practice of the People of the Book. This is limited to in al-Hidayah and chosen by Imam al-Sarakhsi, who said it is the most appropriate. Another view: confusion of his state for those on his right and left. According to the first way, it is absolutely disliked; according to the second, it is not disliked when there is no confusion. In Fath al-Qadir: It is not hidden that the imam's distinction is established and required by the Law concerning place, to the extent that his precedence is obligatory, and the extent here is being in a particular place, and there is no effect because he is opposite the middle of the row, which is desired. Moreover, his standing in non-alignment is disliked, and the extreme is agreement of the two religions in some rulings, and there is nothing strange in that, since the People of the Book only single out the imam to an elevated place, as is said, so there is no resemblance. It may be said that the required distinction of the imam in the Law is achieved by his precedence without standing in another place; when it is possible to distinguish him without resembling the People of the Book, it is determined. Thus, his standing in the mihrab is a resemblance to the People of the Book without need, so it is disliked absolutely. For this reason, al-Walwaji in his Fatawa and the author of al-Tajnis said: If the mosque is narrow with people behind the imam, there is no harm in the imam standing in the arch because it becomes impossible for him; but if it is not narrow, the imam should not stand in the arch because it resembles a difference of places. Meaning: The reality of difference prevents permissibility, and the appearance of difference necessitates dislike. Even though the arch is part of the mosque as is the usual custom, its form and appearance create the appearance of difference. The conclusion is that the apparent ruling from the zahir al-riwayah is dislike of standing in the arch absolutely, whether the imam's state is confusing or not, and whether the arch is part of the mosque or not. Only his prostration in the arch is not disliked if his feet are outside, because the consideration is the feet for the place of prayer, such that their purity is required in one narration, unlike the place of prostration where there are two narrations. Similarly, if one swears not to enter so-and-so's house, he breaks the oath by placing both feet even if the rest of his body is outside; and if game has its feet in the Haram and its head outside, it is game of the Haram and requires compensation. The commentator then addresses an objection: Shaykh Ibrahim al-Halabi mentioned something similar in his commentary, but Ibn Amir Hajj al-Halabi leaned towards supporting what is in Fath al-Qadir, saying that resemblance to the People of the Book is not disliked in everything, etc. He argues that it is not blameworthy, and that the appearance of difference would be contradicted by the case of the imam standing in some other part of the mosque without entering the arch, yet no one calls it disliked, so likewise here. The author responds: The objection can be answered by what the author indicated, that the arch, even though it is part of the mosque, its form and appearance create the appearance of difference, because it is not like other parts of the mosque in that everyone prays in it specifically. It was only made as a marker for the imam's place, and his prostration is in it, not his standing, because it was not built for the imam to stand inside, nor for people to pray in, but only as a marker. Thus, it resembles outside the mosque and becomes like another place, unlike other areas of the mosque. Reflect.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage is a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute about the ruling on the imam standing in the mihrab (the arched niche). The base ruling from Muhammad al-Shaybani is that it is makruh. The reasoning given in al-Hidayah is that it resembles the practice of the People of the Book, who would raise their imam. There are two interpretations: (1) the imam becomes distinct in place, which is like the People of the Book; (2) it causes confusion for the congregation. According to the first, it is absolutely disliked; according to the second, only when confusion arises. The author of Fath al-Qadir argues that distinction of the imam is required by law, so standing in the arch is fine. However, the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq supports the absolute dislike, citing al-Walwaji: if the mosque is crowded, it is permissible out of necessity. The passage also discusses exceptions for prostration in the arch, where the rule is different because only the feet matter. The commentary ends with a rebuttal of an objection, affirming that the arch's form creates the appearance of a separate place, thus dislike remains.

Key Terms
الطاق (al-ṭāq): The arch or niche in the mosque wall, i.e., the mihrab, where the imam stands.
تشبه بأهل الكتاب (tashabbuh bi-ahl al-kitāb): Resembling the People of the Book, a reason for dislike in certain acts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is it permissible for the imam to stand in the mihrab?
A) If the mosque is very spacious
B) If the congregation might be confused
C) If the mosque is crowded with people behind the imam
D) It is always permissible

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school generally holds that the imam standing in the mihrab is makruh unless necessary, due to resemblance to the People of the Book.

Ruling on Imam Standing on a Raised Platform
Explains the ruling on the imam standing alone on a raised platform (dakkan) with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imam standing on a raised platform, explain the evidence from the hadith, and distinguish the positions of al-Tahawi and Qadikhan on the height threshold.

Core Idea
The imam must not stand higher than the congregation to avoid resemblance to non-Muslims.

This lesson examines a specific issue in congregational prayer: the imam standing on a raised platform (dakkan). The ruling is derived from a prophetic prohibition and the principle of avoiding resemblance to other faiths. Scholars differ on the exact height that triggers dislike, reflecting careful analysis of the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Identify the act being ruled upon: the imam standing alone on a raised platform. Determine the hukm level from the text.
The act is makruh, but the degree (tanzih vs tahrim) is debated.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary evidence: the hadith of al-Hakim (marfu') that prohibits the imam standing above the congregation.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyse how the prohibition (نهى) indicates the ruling. The command to avoid implies karahah. The reason given (tashabbuh) suggests the prohibition is for tanzih, but the text itself may indicate tahrim.
The tension between the hadith text and its explanation is noted by al-Ramli.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Identify the differing positions: al-Tahawi restricts to a man's stature, Qadikhan to a cubit, and others hold absolute dislike regardless of height.
No single mufta bihi is given; the author leaves it for reflection.
5
Determine the practical application
Understand that the relied-upon position is that the platform should not be significantly elevated, with details varying. The key principle is to avoid any height that creates separation or resemblance.
In practice, the imam should be at the same level as the congregation or only slightly elevated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وانفراد الإمام على الدكان وعكسه أما الأول فلحديث الحاكم مرفوعاً: رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن يقوم الإمام فوق ويبقى الناس خلفه. وعللوه بأنه تشبه بأهل الكتاب فإنهم يتخذون لإمامهم دكاناً . أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان الدكان قدر قامة الرجل أو دون ذلك وهو ظاهر الرواية. وصححه في البدائع لإطلاق النهي وقيده الطحاوي بقدر القامة ونفى الكراهة فيما دونه. وقال قاضيخان في شرح الجامع الصغير : إنه مقدر بذراع اعتباراً بالسترة وعليه
قوله : (وعللوه) قال الرملي : هذا التعليل يقتضي أنها تنزيهية والحديث المتقدم يقتضي أنها تحريمية إلا أن يوجد صارف تأمل.
His saying: (and the imam's standing alone on the platform and its opposite). As for the first, due to the hadith of al-Hakim raised to the Prophet: 'The Messenger of Allah forbade that the imam stand above while the people remain behind him.' And they explained it as resemblance to the People of the Book, for they take a platform for their imam. It was left general, so it includes whether the platform is the height of a man or less, and that is the apparent narration. And he authenticated it in al-Badai due to the general prohibition, but al-Tahawi restricted it to the height of a man and negated dislike for less. Qadikhan said in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir: It is estimated by a cubit, considering the sutra. Then the commentator says: His saying: (and they explained it) al-Ramli said: This explanation indicates that it is tanzih (lesser dislike), while the preceding hadith indicates that it is tahrim (prohibitory), unless there is a diverting factor. Reflect.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage rules on the imam standing on a raised platform (dakkan). The hadith from al-Hakim prohibits the imam standing higher than the congregation. The reasoning is resemblance to the People of the Book. There are differing interpretations: some hold it is disliked absolutely regardless of height, while al-Tahawi restricts the prohibition to a height of a man's stature, and Qadikhan suggests a cubit as the threshold. The author notes that the explanation (tashabbuh) suggests the dislike is tanzih, but the text of the hadith itself may indicate tahrim. The final note from al-Ramli acknowledges the tension between the two levels and leaves it as needing reflection.

Key Terms
الدكان (al-dukkān): A raised platform or seat for the imam, resembling those used by People of the Book.
التشبه (al-tashabbuh): Resemblance or imitation, here specifically of the People of the Book, which forms the reasoning behind the prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did al-Tahawi specify regarding the platform's height?
A) It is always disliked
B) Dislike only if taller than a man's stature
C) It is permissible
D) It is estimated by a cubit

Key Takeaway
The hanafi ruling on the imam's platform is makruh, with the degree varying by height; the principle is to avoid resemblance to non-Muslims, and caution is advised.

Ruling on Wearing Clothes with Images in Prayer
States the ruling that wearing garments with images is disliked in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding images during prayer and identify the positions where images are disliked.

Core Idea
During prayer, images on clothing or nearby are disliked (makruh) due to distraction.

This lesson presents a concise ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding images in the prayer space. The text establishes that it is disliked for the worshiper to wear garments bearing images, or to have such images above, in front, or beside him. Understanding this ruling helps maintain the proper solemnity of salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Determine what action or situation is being ruled upon: wearing a garment with images, or having images in specific locations during prayer.
The act includes both wearing and having images in the immediate surroundings.
2
Determine the legal classification
Classify the ruling according to Hanafi hukm levels. Here the text implies makruh (disliked).
Makruh tanzihi (disliked, not prohibited) is typical for images in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Recognize the rationale
Understand why images are disliked in salah: they distract the worshiper and resemble idolatrous practices.
The rationale is not explicit in this short text but is established in broader Hanafi works.
4
Note the scope
The ruling applies to the imam and any worshiper, and includes images on clothing as well as images placed above, in front, or beside the prayer area.
‘Above his head or between his hands or alongside him’ covers all directions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وعكسه ولبس ثوب فيه تصاوير وإن يكون فوق رأسه أو بين يديه أو بحذائه)
His saying: (and its opposite, and wearing a garment containing images, and that they be above his head or in front of him or alongside him)
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This is a statement of a ruling: it is disliked for the imam (or any worshipper) to wear a garment that has images, or to have such images above him, in front of him, or beside him during prayer. The text is from the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, and the commentator is about to explain it, but the explanation is not present in this portion. The underlying principle is that images in the prayer space are distracting and resemble idolatry, hence disliked. The phrase 'its opposite' refers to the previous discussion about the imam on the platform, i.e., he should not stand behind the congregation either. This lesson simply records the ruling as a memorization anchor.

Key Terms
تصاوير (taṣāwīr): Images or pictures, whether on clothing or as objects, that are disliked in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following actions is considered makruh in prayer?
A) Wearing a plain white garment.
B) Having a picture of a horse on your shirt.
C) Facing the qibla.
D) Reciting Quran aloud.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, it is disliked (makruh) to wear clothes with animate images or to have such images in the prayer space during salah, but the prayer remains valid.

Imam Standing Alone on a Raised Platform
Commentary on the ruling of imam standing alone on a platform

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imam standing alone on a raised platform, identify the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf, and apply the exceptions for necessity.

Core Idea
The imam standing alone on a platform is disliked due to resemblance to People of the Book, but exceptions exist for crowding and teaching.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a practical issue in congregation prayer: the imam standing on a raised platform. The Hanafi school generally considers this disliked (makruh) because it resembles the practices of the People of the Book, but there are important differences of opinion among Hanafi scholars regarding height and circumstances. Understanding these nuances helps ensure the prayer is performed without unnecessary dislike.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the imam standing alone on a raised platform (dakkan) during prayer. The apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) rules it as makruh (disliked).
The text distinguishes between the imam on platform and congregation on platform.
2
Locate the dalil
A hadith narrated by al-Hakim from the Prophet prohibiting the imam from standing above the congregation.
The hadith is used as proof.
3
Analyze the reasoning
The dislike is due to resemblance to the People of the Book (tashabbuh bi-ahl al-kitab) and the semblance of difference in place.
The reason is cited from the scholars.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Al-Tahawi restricts the dislike to a platform of man's height or more; Qadi Khan estimates a cubit. The text shows disagreement about the threshold.
The Narration from al-Tahawi is stricter.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and exceptions
The author leans toward the apparent narration (absolute dislike) but notes exceptions for necessity (crowding on Friday/Eid) and when the imam intends to teach.
The ruling is not absolute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدكان
كتاب الصلاة باب ما يفسد الصلاة وما يكره فيها
وعكسه ولبس ثوب فيه تصاوير وإن يكون فوق رأسه أو بين يديه أو بحذائه
يخصون الإمام بالمكان المرتفع على ما قيل فلا تشبه .اهـ. وقد يقال إن امتياز الإمام المطلوب في الشرع حاصل بتقدمه من غير أن يقف في مكان آخر، فمتى أمكن تمييزه من غير تشبه بأهل الكتاب تعين، فحينئذ وقوفه في المحراب تشبه بأهل الكتاب لغير حاجة فكره مطلقاً ولهذا قال الولوالجي في فتاواه وصاحب التجنيس : إذا ضاق المسجد بمن خلف الإمام على القوم لا بأس بأن يقوم الإمام في الطاق لأنه تعذر الأمر عليه، وإن لم يضق المسجد بمن خلف الإمام لا ينبغي للإمام أن يقوم في الطاق لأنه يشبه تباين المكانين .اهـ. يعني وحقيقة اختلاف المكان تمنع الجواز فشبهة الاختلاف توجب الكراهة وهو وإن كان المحراب من المسجد كما العادة المستمرة فصورته وهيئته اقتضت شبهة الاختلاف فالحاصل أن مقتضى ظاهر الرواية كراهة قيامه في المحراب مطلقاً، سواء اشتبه حال الإمام أو لا، وسواء كان المحراب من المسجد أم لا . وإنما لم يكره سجوده في المحراب إذا كان قدماه خارجه لأن العبرة للقدم في مكان الصلاة حتى تشترط طهارته رواية واحدة بخلاف مكان السجود إذ فيه روايتان. وكذا لو حلف لا يدخل دار فلان يحنث بوضع القدمين وإن كان باقي بدنه خارجها، والصيد إذا كان رجلاه في الحرم ورأسه خارج منه فهو صيد الحرم ففيه الجزاء.
هي
نهی
قوله (وانفراد الإمام على الدكان وعكسه أما الأول فلحديث الحاكم مرفوعاً: رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن يقوم الإمام فوق ويبقى الناس خلفه. وعللوه بأنه تشبه بأهل الكتاب فإنهم يتخذون لإمامهم دكاناً . أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان الدكان قدر قامة الرجل أو دون ذلك وهو ظاهر الرواية. وصححه في البدائع لإطلاق النهي وقيده الطحاوي بقدر القامة ونفى الكراهة فيما دونه. وقال قاضيخان في شرح الجامع الصغير : إنه مقدر بذراع اعتباراً بالسترة وعليه
قوله : (وقد يقال الخ ذكر نحوه الشيخ إبراهيم الحلبي في شرحه على المنية لكن جنح ابن أمير
المسجد
حاج الحلبي في شرحه على المنية إلى تأييد ما في فتح القدير حيث قال: قلت ويؤيده ما قدمناه عن قاضيخان أن التشبه بأهل الكتاب لا يكره في كل شيء الخ. وليس هذا من المذموم في شيء وكونه يشبه اختلاف المكانين وحقيقة الاختلاف تمنع الجواز فشبهة الاختلاف توجب الكراهة يعارض بما لو تقدم في بعض بقاع المسجد على القوم من غير أن يدخل المحراب ولا قائل بالكراهة فيه فكذا هنا اهـ . قلت : يجاب عن المعارضة المذكورة بما أشار إليه المؤلف من أن المحراب وإن كان من لكن صورته وهيئته تقتضي شبهة اختلاف المكان لأنه ليس كبقيه بقاع المسجد من حيث إنه يصلي فيه بخصوصه كل أحد، وإنما جعل علامة لمكان وقوف الإمام وأن يكون سجوده فيه لا قيامه لأنه لم يبن لأن يقوم الإمام في داخله ولا لأن يصلي فيه الناس وإنما هو علامة كما قلنا فأشبه خارج المسجد فصار بمنزلة مكان آخر بخلاف بقية بقاع المسجد تأمل قوله : (وعللوه) قال الرملي : هذا التعليل يقتضي أنها تنزيهية والحديث المتقدم يقتضي أنها تحريمية إلا أن يوجد صارف تأمل.

كتاب الصلاة باب ما يفسد الصلاة وما يكره فيها
٤٧
الاعتماد، وفي غاية البيان وهو الصحيح، وفي فتح القدير وهو المختار لكن قال: الأوجه الإطلاق وهو ما يقع به الامتياز لأن الموجب وهو شبه الإزدراء يتحقق فيه غير مقتصر على قدر الذراع اهـ. فالحاصل أن التصحيح قد اختلف والأولى العمل بظاهر الرواية وإطلاق الحديث، وأما عكسه وهو انفراد القوم على الدكان بأن يكون الإمام أسفل فهو مكروه أيضاً في ظاهر الرواية وروى الطحاوي عن أصحابنا أنه لا يكره لأن الموجب للكراهة التشبه بأهل الكتاب ولا تشبه هنا لأن مكان إمامهم لا يكون أسفل وجواب ظاهر الرواية أقرب إلى الصواب لأن كراهة كون المكان أرفع كان معلولاً بعلتين : التشبه بأهل الكتاب ووجود بعض المفسد وهو اختلاف المكان وههنا وجدت إحدى العلتين وهي وجود بعض المخالفة. كذا في البدائع. ومن المشايخ من علل الكراهة في الثانية بما في ذلك من شبه الإزدراء بالإمام ولعله أولى، وعلى ما ذكره الطحاوي من عدم الكراهة مشى قاضيخان في فتاواه وعزاه إلى النوادر وقال : وعليه عامة المشايخ .اهـ. وهذا كله عند عدم العذر، أما عند العذر كما في الجمعة والعيدين فإن القوم يقومون على الرفوف والإمام على الأرض ولم يكره ذلك لضيق المكان. كذا في النهاية. وذكر في شرح منية المصلي : وهل يدخل في الحاجة في حق الإمام إرادة تعليم المأمومين أعمال الصلاة وفي حق المأمومين إرادة تبليغ انتقالات الإمام عند اتساع وكثرة المصلين؟ فعند الشافعي نعم قيل وهو رواية عن أبي حنيفة اهـ. قيد بالانفراد لأنه لو قام بعض القوم مع الإمام قيل يكره والأصح أنه لا يكره وبه جرت العادة في جوامع المسلمين في أغلب الأمصار كذا في المحيط. وذكر في البدائع أن من اعتبر معنى التشبه قال لا يكره وهو قياس رواية الطحاوي لزوال معنى التشبه لأن أهل الكتاب لا يشاركون الإمام المكان، ومن اعتبر وجود بعض المفسد قال يكره وهو قياس ظاهر الرواية لوجود بعض في المكان .اهـ. وفيه نظر لا يخفى قوله ولبس ثوب فيه تصاوير) لأنه يشبه حامل الصنم فيكره. وفي الخلاصة وتكره التصاوير على الثوب صلى فيه أو لم يصل اهـ. وهذه
المكان
في
المخالفة
قوله : (وذكر في شرح منية المصلي (الخ أقول في المعراج ما نصه : وبقولنا قال الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى إلا إذا أراد الإمام تعليم القوم أفعال الصلاة أو أراد المأموم تبليغ القوم فحينئذ لا يكره عندنا اهـ. قوله : (لأنه لو قام بعض القوم الظاهر أن المراد بالبعض جماعة من القوم لا واحد لما في الدر المختار في باب الإمامة من أنه لو قام واحد بجنب الإمام وخلفه صف كره إجماعاً قوله : (فينبغي أن يكون حراماً) تفريع على قوله وظاهر كلام النووي الخ» ثم المتبادر من سياقه كلام النووي والتفريع عليه أن مراده الاعتراض على ما نقله عن الخلاصة من قوله وتكره التصاوير على الثوب الخ» ويمكن أن يقال : ليس مراد الخلاصة تصوير التصاوير بل استعمالها أي استعمال الثوب التي هي فيه فيساوي كلام المصنف، ويدل على أن هذا هو المراد قول الخلاصة بعد عبارته السابقة، أما إذا كان في يده
The platform. Book of prayer, chapter on what nullifies prayer and what is disliked therein. And its opposite, and wearing a garment containing images, and if it is above his head or in front of him or alongside him. They specify the imam with the elevated place, as was said, so do not resemble. End. And it may be said that the distinction of the imam required in the law is achieved by his advancement without standing in another place, so when his distinction is possible without resembling the People of the Book, it is determined. So then his standing in the mihrab is resembling the People of the Book without need, so it is disliked absolutely. And for this reason al-Walwaliji said in his Fatawa and the author of al-Tajnis: When the mosque is crowded by those behind the imam over the congregation, there is no harm in the imam standing in the niche because the matter is difficult for him, and if the mosque is not crowded by those behind the imam, the imam should not stand in the niche because it resembles the difference of two places. End. Meaning that the actual difference of place prevents permissibility, so the semblance of difference necessitates dislike. And even if the mihrab is part of the mosque as is the continuous custom, its form and shape entail the semblance of difference. So the conclusion is that the requirement of the apparent narration is the dislike of his standing in the mihrab absolutely, whether the condition of the imam is ambiguous or not, and whether the mihrab is part of the mosque or not. And his prostration in the mihrab is not disliked if his feet are outside it because consideration is for the feet in the place of prayer, to the extent that its purity is required in one narration, unlike the place of prostration, as there are two narrations. Similarly, if he swears not to enter so-and-so's house, he breaks his oath by placing his feet even if the rest of his body is outside it. And game, if its two legs are in the sanctuary and its head is outside, it is game of the sanctuary, so there is a penalty for it. [Stray: she, prohibition]. His statement: (And the imam's being alone on the platform and its opposite). As for the first, due to the hadith of al-Hakim raised: The Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, [ordered] that the imam should not stand above while the people remain behind him. And they gave the reason that it is resembling the People of the Book, for they take a platform for their imam. He made it absolute, so it includes whether the platform is the length of a man or less, and this is the apparent narration. And al-Bada'i' corrected it due to the absolute prohibition, while al-Tahawi restricted it to the length of a man and denied dislike in less than that. And Qadi Khan said in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir: It is estimated by a cubit, considering the sutra, and upon it is reliance. His statement: (And it may be said... etc.) Sheikh Ibrahim al-Halabi mentioned something similar in his commentary on al-Munya, but Ibn Amir Hajj al-Halabi inclined in his commentary on al-Munya to support what is in Fath al-Qadir, where he said: I say, and it is supported by what we presented from Qadi Khan that resemblance to the People of the Book is not disliked in everything, etc. And this is not at all blameworthy. And its being like the difference of two places and the actual difference preventing permissibility, so the semblance of difference necessitating dislike, is countered by what if he advanced in some area of the mosque over the congregation without entering the mihrab, and no one says it is disliked there, so likewise here. End. I say: The aforementioned objection is answered by what the author indicated, that the mihrab, even though it is part of the mosque, its form and shape imply the semblance of difference of place because it is not like other areas of the mosque, in that everyone prays in it specifically. Rather, it is made as a sign for the place of the imam's standing and that his prostration should be in it, not his standing, because it was not built for the imam to stand inside it, nor for the people to pray in it. Rather, it is a sign as we said, so it resembles the outside of the mosque and becomes like another place, unlike other areas of the mosque. Contemplate. His statement: (And they gave the reason). Al-Ramli said: This reasoning implies that it is a prohibitory dislike, and the preceding hadith implies that it is a prohbition, unless there is a diverting factor. Contemplate. [Page 47] Reliance, and in Ghayat al-Bayan it is correct, and in Fath al-Qadir it is the chosen, but he said: The most correct is the absolute, which is what achieves distinction, because the cause, which is the semblance of contempt, is realized in it, not limited to the measure of a cubit. End. So the conclusion is that the correction has differed, and the better is to act upon the apparent narration and the absolute hadith. As for its opposite, which is the congregation being alone on the platform, meaning the imam is below, it is also disliked in the apparent narration. Al-Tahawi narrated from our companions that it is not disliked, because the cause for dislike is resemblance to the People of the Book, and there is no resemblance here because the place of their imam is not below. And the answer of the apparent narration is closer to correctness, because the dislike of the place being higher was caused by two causes: resemblance to the People of the Book and the existence of some corruption, which is difference of place. And here one of the two causes is found, which is the existence of some opposition. Thus in al-Bada'i'. And some shaykhs gave the reason for dislike in the second by the semblance of contempt for the imam, and perhaps that is better. And according to what al-Tahawi mentioned of the absence of dislike, Qadi Khan followed in his Fatawa and attributed it to al-Nawadir and said: And upon it are the majority of shaykhs. End. And all this is in the absence of an excuse; when there is an excuse, such as on Friday and the two Eids, the congregation stands on the shelves and the imam on the ground, and that is not disliked due to the narrowness of the place. Thus in al-Nihaya. And it is mentioned in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli: And does need include in the right of the imam the intention to teach the congregation the actions of prayer, and in the right of the congregation the intention to convey the transitions of the imam when the mosque is spacious and the worshippers are many? According to al-Shafi'i, yes, and it is said it is a narration from Abu Hanifa. End. He restricted it to the imam being alone, because if some of the congregation stand with the imam, it is said it is disliked, and the correct is that it is not disliked, and this is the custom in the congregational mosques of Muslims in most cities. Thus in al-Muhit. And it is mentioned in al-Bada'i' that whoever considers the meaning of resemblance says it is not disliked, and this is the analogy of al-Tahawi's narration due to the removal of the meaning of resemblance, because the People of the Book do not share the place with the imam. And whoever considers the existence of some corruption says it is disliked, and this is the analogy of the apparent narration due to the existence of some opposition in the place. End. And there is a hidden point. His statement: (and wearing a garment containing images) because it resembles the carrier of an idol, so it is disliked. And in al-Khulasa: And images on a garment are disliked, whether one prays in it or not. End. And these [stray: the place, in, the opposition]. His statement: (and it is mentioned in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli etc.) I say in al-Mi'raj: The text of it: And by our saying al-Shafi'i, may God have mercy on him, said, except if the imam intends to teach the congregation the actions of prayer or the follower intends to convey to the congregation, then it is not disliked according to us. End. His statement: (because if some of the congregation stood) the apparent is that by 'some' is meant a group of the congregation, not one, because in al-Durr al-Mukhtar in the chapter of imamate, that if one stands next to the imam and behind him a row, it is disliked by consensus. His statement: (so it should be forbidden) is a branching from his statement and the apparent of al-Nawawi's speech etc. Then the understood from his context is al-Nawawi's speech and the branching upon it, that his intention is objection to what he transmitted from al-Khulasa, his statement: 'and images on a garment are disliked'. And it can be said: The intention of al-Khulasa is not the depiction of images, but their use, i.e., the use of the garment in which they are, so it equals the author's speech. And it is indicated that this is the intended meaning by the statement of al-Khulasa after his previous expression: 'as for if it is in his hand...'
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addressing two separate but related rulings within the chapter on what nullifies or is disliked in prayer. The first ruling concerns the imam standing alone on a raised platform (dakkan). The second concerns wearing a garment with images during prayer. The commentary begins by explaining the general dislike of the imam standing in the mihrab (niche) due to resemblance to the People of the Book. The author notes that the mihrab, though part of the mosque, has a form that suggests a separate place, leading to dislike. However, exceptions exist for necessity, such as crowding. A hadith from al-Hakim is cited as proof for the prohibition of the imam standing above the congregation. The commentary then details an intra-Hanafi dispute: the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) holds absolute dislike for the imam on a platform, but al-Tahawi restricts it to the height of a man, and others estimate a cubit. The opposite case—congregation on the platform with the imam below—is also generally disliked, though al-Tahawi reports from the Nawadir that it is not disliked because the cause (resemblance to People of the Book) is absent. The author weighs the positions, favoring the apparent narration for the first ruling, but noting the common practice of shaykhs on the opposite. Exceptions for Friday and Eid prayers due to space are noted, as well as the permissibility if the imam intends to teach. The second ruling on garments with images is simpler: wearing such a garment is disliked because it resembles carrying an idol. Al-Khulasa adds that images on a garment are disliked whether or not one prays in it. The commentary ends with further discussion on the interpretation of al-Khulasa's intention, stating that it refers to using the garment with images, not the act of depiction itself. The passage cuts off mid-sentence during this discussion.

Key Terms
الدكان (al-dakkan): A raised platform or bench upon which the imam stands alone during prayer.
المحراب (al-mihrab): A niche in the mosque indicating the qibla, where the imam stands. The text discusses its form leading to semblance of separate place.
التشبه بأهل الكتاب (al-tashabbuh bi-ahl al-kitab): Imitating the practices of Jews and Christians. A reason for dislike in these rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on the congregation alone standing on a raised platform while the imam stands below?
A) It is always permissible and not disliked.
B) In the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) it is disliked, but according to al-Tahawi's narration from the Nawadir it is not disliked.
C) It is completely forbidden (haram) because it resembles the People of the Book.
D) It is only disliked if the platform is higher than a cubit.

Key Takeaway
The imam's standing on a raised platform in prayer is disliked in the Hanafi school, but exceptions exist for necessity and teaching.

Wearing Garments with Images in Prayer
Ruling on garments with images in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wearing a garment containing images during prayer and explain the reasoning behind the dislike.

Core Idea
Wearing a garment with images in prayer is disliked because it resembles carrying an idol.

This part of the passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses another disliked matter in prayer: wearing clothes with pictures or images. The Hanafi school rules it as makruh because it resembles the act of carrying an idol. The commentator clarifies that this applies to using the garment, not to the act of creating the image itself. Although the source text is incomplete, the ruling is clear and widely accepted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wearing a garment containing images during prayer. The ruling is that it is disliked (makruh).
The text says 'يكره' (it is disliked).
2
Locate the reasoning
The dislike is because it resembles carrying an idol (حامل الصنم).
The analogy is between the garment and an idol.
3
Analyze the scope
Al-Khulasa states that images on a garment are disliked whether or not one prays in it, indicating the dislike is for the use of such garments.
The commentator clarifies that the dislike is for use, not depiction.
4
Note any ikhtilaf
The passage ends with a discussion whether the ruling is about depiction or use, and the author sides with use. There is a brief mention of a Shafi'i exception for teaching.
The source cuts off; the main ruling stands.

كتاب الصلاة باب ما يفسد الصلاة وما يكره فيها
وعكسه ولبس ثوب فيه تصاوير وإن يكون فوق رأسه أو بين يديه أو بحذائه
يخصون الإمام بالمكان المرتفع على ما قيل فلا تشبه .اهـ. وقد يقال إن امتياز الإمام المطلوب في الشرع حاصل بتقدمه من غير أن يقف في مكان آخر، فمتى أمكن تمييزه من غير تشبه بأهل الكتاب تعين، فحينئذ وقوفه في المحراب تشبه بأهل الكتاب لغير حاجة فكره مطلقاً ولهذا قال الولوالجي في فتاواه وصاحب التجنيس : إذا ضاق المسجد بمن خلف الإمام على القوم لا بأس بأن يقوم الإمام في الطاق لأنه تعذر الأمر عليه، وإن لم يضق المسجد بمن خلف الإمام لا ينبغي للإمام أن يقوم في الطاق لأنه يشبه تباين المكانين .اهـ. يعني وحقيقة اختلاف المكان تمنع الجواز فشبهة الاختلاف توجب الكراهة وهو وإن كان المحراب من المسجد كما العادة المستمرة فصورته وهيئته اقتضت شبهة الاختلاف فالحاصل أن مقتضى ظاهر الرواية كراهة قيامه في المحراب مطلقاً، سواء اشتبه حال الإمام أو لا، وسواء كان المحراب من المسجد أم لا . وإنما لم يكره سجوده في المحراب إذا كان قدماه خارجه لأن العبرة للقدم في مكان الصلاة حتى تشترط طهارته رواية واحدة بخلاف مكان السجود إذ فيه روايتان. وكذا لو حلف لا يدخل دار فلان يحنث بوضع القدمين وإن كان باقي بدنه خارجها، والصيد إذا كان رجلاه في الحرم ورأسه خارج منه فهو صيد الحرم ففيه الجزاء.

نهی
قوله (وانفراد الإمام على الدكان وعكسه أما الأول فلحديث الحاكم مرفوعاً: رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن يقوم الإمام فوق ويبقى الناس خلفه. وعللوه بأنه تشبه بأهل الكتاب فإنهم يتخذون لإمامهم دكاناً . أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان الدكان قدر قامة الرجل أو دون ذلك وهو ظاهر الرواية. وصححه في البدائع لإطلاق النهي وقيده الطحاوي بقدر القامة ونفى الكراهة فيما دونه. وقال قاضيخان في شرح الجامع الصغير : إنه مقدر بذراع اعتباراً بالسترة وعليه
قوله : (وقد يقال الخ ذكر نحوه الشيخ إبراهيم الحلبي في شرحه على المنية لكن جنح ابن أمير
المسجد
حاج الحلبي في شرحه على المنية إلى تأييد ما في فتح القدير حيث قال: قلت ويؤيده ما قدمناه عن قاضيخان أن التشبه بأهل الكتاب لا يكره في كل شيء الخ. وليس هذا من المذموم في شيء وكونه يشبه اختلاف المكانين وحقيقة الاختلاف تمنع الجواز فشبهة الاختلاف توجب الكراهة يعارض بما لو تقدم في بعض بقاع المسجد على القوم من غير أن يدخل المحراب ولا قائل بالكراهة فيه فكذا هنا اهـ . قلت : يجاب عن المعارضة المذكورة بما أشار إليه المؤلف من أن المحراب وإن كان من لكن صورته وهيئته تقتضي شبهة اختلاف المكان لأنه ليس كبقيه بقاع المسجد من حيث إنه يصلي فيه بخصوصه كل أحد، وإنما جعل علامة لمكان وقوف الإمام وأن يكون سجوده فيه لا قيامه لأنه لم يبن لأن يقوم الإمام في داخله ولا لأن يصلي فيه الناس وإنما هو علامة كما قلنا فأشبه خارج المسجد فصار بمنزلة مكان آخر بخلاف بقية بقاع المسجد تأمل قوله : (وعللوه) قال الرملي : هذا التعليل يقتضي أنها تنزيهية والحديث المتقدم يقتضي أنها تحريمية إلا أن يوجد صارف تأمل.

كتاب الصلاة باب ما يفسد الصلاة وما يكره فيها
٤٧
الاعتماد، وفي غاية البيان وهو الصحيح، وفي فتح القدير وهو المختار لكن قال: الأوجه الإطلاق وهو ما يقع به الامتياز لأن الموجب وهو شبه الإزدراء يتحقق فيه غير مقتصر على قدر الذراع اهـ. فالحاصل أن التصحيح قد اختلف والأولى العمل بظاهر الرواية وإطلاق الحديث، وأما عكسه وهو انفراد القوم على الدكان بأن يكون الإمام أسفل فهو مكروه أيضاً في ظاهر الرواية وروى الطحاوي عن أصحابنا أنه لا يكره لأن الموجب للكراهة التشبه بأهل الكتاب ولا تشبه هنا لأن مكان إمامهم لا يكون أسفل وجواب ظاهر الرواية أقرب إلى الصواب لأن كراهة كون المكان أرفع كان معلولاً بعلتين : التشبه بأهل الكتاب ووجود بعض المفسد وهو اختلاف المكان وههنا وجدت إحدى العلتين وهي وجود بعض المخالفة. كذا في البدائع. ومن المشايخ من علل الكراهة في الثانية بما في ذلك من شبه الإزدراء بالإمام ولعله أولى، وعلى ما ذكره الطحاوي من عدم الكراهة مشى قاضيخان في فتاواه وعزاه إلى النوادر وقال : وعليه عامة المشايخ .اهـ. وهذا كله عند عدم العذر، أما عند العذر كما في الجمعة والعيدين فإن القوم يقومون على الرفوف والإمام على الأرض ولم يكره ذلك لضيق المكان. كذا في النهاية. وذكر في شرح منية المصلي : وهل يدخل في الحاجة في حق الإمام إرادة تعليم المأمومين أعمال الصلاة وفي حق المأمومين إرادة تبليغ انتقالات الإمام عند اتساع وكثرة المصلين؟ فعند الشافعي نعم قيل وهو رواية عن أبي حنيفة اهـ. قيد بالانفراد لأنه لو قام بعض القوم مع الإمام قيل يكره والأصح أنه لا يكره وبه جرت العادة في جوامع المسلمين في أغلب الأمصار كذا في المحيط. وذكر في البدائع أن من اعتبر معنى التشبه قال لا يكره وهو قياس رواية الطحاوي لزوال معنى التشبه لأن أهل الكتاب لا يشاركون الإمام المكان، ومن اعتبر وجود بعض المفسد قال يكره وهو قياس ظاهر الرواية لوجود بعض في المكان .اهـ. وفيه نظر لا يخفى قوله ولبس ثوب فيه تصاوير) لأنه يشبه حامل الصنم فيكره. وفي الخلاصة وتكره التصاوير على الثوب صلى فيه أو لم يصل اهـ. وهذه
المكان
في
المخالفة
قوله : (وذكر في شرح منية المصلي (الخ أقول في المعراج ما نصه : وبقولنا قال الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى إلا إذا أراد الإمام تعليم القوم أفعال الصلاة أو أراد المأموم تبليغ القوم فحينئذ لا يكره عندنا اهـ. قوله : (لأنه لو قام بعض القوم الظاهر أن المراد بالبعض جماعة من القوم لا واحد لما في الدر المختار في باب الإمامة من أنه لو قام واحد بجنب الإمام وخلفه صف كره إجماعاً قوله : (فينبغي أن يكون حراماً) تفريع على قوله وظاهر كلام النووي الخ» ثم المتبادر من سياقه كلام النووي والتفريع عليه أن مراده الاعتراض على ما نقله عن الخلاصة من قوله وتكره التصاوير على الثوب الخ» ويمكن أن يقال : ليس مراد الخلاصة تصوير التصاوير بل استعمالها أي استعمال الثوب التي هي فيه فيساوي كلام المصنف، ويدل على أن هذا هو المراد قول الخلاصة بعد عبارته السابقة، أما إذا كان في يده
The platform. Book of prayer, chapter on what nullifies prayer and what is disliked therein. And its opposite, and wearing a garment containing images, and if it is above his head or in front of him or alongside him. They specify the imam with the elevated place, as was said, so do not resemble. End. And it may be said that the distinction of the imam required in the law is achieved by his advancement without standing in another place, so when his distinction is possible without resembling the People of the Book, it is determined. So then his standing in the mihrab is resembling the People of the Book without need, so it is disliked absolutely. And for this reason al-Walwaliji said in his Fatawa and the author of al-Tajnis: When the mosque is crowded by those behind the imam over the congregation, there is no harm in the imam standing in the niche because the matter is difficult for him, and if the mosque is not crowded by those behind the imam, the imam should not stand in the niche because it resembles the difference of two places. End. Meaning that the actual difference of place prevents permissibility, so the semblance of difference necessitates dislike. And even if the mihrab is part of the mosque as is the continuous custom, its form and shape entail the semblance of difference. So the conclusion is that the requirement of the apparent narration is the dislike of his standing in the mihrab absolutely, whether the condition of the imam is ambiguous or not, and whether the mihrab is part of the mosque or not. And his prostration in the mihrab is not disliked if his feet are outside it because consideration is for the feet in the place of prayer, to the extent that its purity is required in one narration, unlike the place of prostration, as there are two narrations. Similarly, if he swears not to enter so-and-so's house, he breaks his oath by placing his feet even if the rest of his body is outside it. And game, if its two legs are in the sanctuary and its head is outside, it is game of the sanctuary, so there is a penalty for it. [Stray: she, prohibition]. His statement: (And the imam's being alone on the platform and its opposite). As for the first, due to the hadith of al-Hakim raised: The Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, [ordered] that the imam should not stand above while the people remain behind him. And they gave the reason that it is resembling the People of the Book, for they take a platform for their imam. He made it absolute, so it includes whether the platform is the length of a man or less, and this is the apparent narration. And al-Bada'i' corrected it due to the absolute prohibition, while al-Tahawi restricted it to the length of a man and denied dislike in less than that. And Qadi Khan said in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir: It is estimated by a cubit, considering the sutra, and upon it is reliance. His statement: (And it may be said... etc.) Sheikh Ibrahim al-Halabi mentioned something similar in his commentary on al-Munya, but Ibn Amir Hajj al-Halabi inclined in his commentary on al-Munya to support what is in Fath al-Qadir, where he said: I say, and it is supported by what we presented from Qadi Khan that resemblance to the People of the Book is not disliked in everything, etc. And this is not at all blameworthy. And its being like the difference of two places and the actual difference preventing permissibility, so the semblance of difference necessitating dislike, is countered by what if he advanced in some area of the mosque over the congregation without entering the mihrab, and no one says it is disliked there, so likewise here. End. I say: The aforementioned objection is answered by what the author indicated, that the mihrab, even though it is part of the mosque, its form and shape imply the semblance of difference of place because it is not like other areas of the mosque, in that everyone prays in it specifically. Rather, it is made as a sign for the place of the imam's standing and that his prostration should be in it, not his standing, because it was not built for the imam to stand inside it, nor for the people to pray in it. Rather, it is a sign as we said, so it resembles the outside of the mosque and becomes like another place, unlike other areas of the mosque. Contemplate. His statement: (And they gave the reason). Al-Ramli said: This reasoning implies that it is a prohibitory dislike, and the preceding hadith implies that it is a prohbition, unless there is a diverting factor. Contemplate. [Page 47] Reliance, and in Ghayat al-Bayan it is correct, and in Fath al-Qadir it is the chosen, but he said: The most correct is the absolute, which is what achieves distinction, because the cause, which is the semblance of contempt, is realized in it, not limited to the measure of a cubit. End. So the conclusion is that the correction has differed, and the better is to act upon the apparent narration and the absolute hadith. As for its opposite, which is the congregation being alone on the platform, meaning the imam is below, it is also disliked in the apparent narration. Al-Tahawi narrated from our companions that it is not disliked, because the cause for dislike is resemblance to the People of the Book, and there is no resemblance here because the place of their imam is not below. And the answer of the apparent narration is closer to correctness, because the dislike of the place being higher was caused by two causes: resemblance to the People of the Book and the existence of some corruption, which is difference of place. And here one of the two causes is found, which is the existence of some opposition. Thus in al-Bada'i'. And some shaykhs gave the reason for dislike in the second by the semblance of contempt for the imam, and perhaps that is better. And according to what al-Tahawi mentioned of the absence of dislike, Qadi Khan followed in his Fatawa and attributed it to al-Nawadir and said: And upon it are the majority of shaykhs. End. And all this is in the absence of an excuse; when there is an excuse, such as on Friday and the two Eids, the congregation stands on the shelves and the imam on the ground, and that is not disliked due to the narrowness of the place. Thus in al-Nihaya. And it is mentioned in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli: And does need include in the right of the imam the intention to teach the congregation the actions of prayer, and in the right of the congregation the intention to convey the transitions of the imam when the mosque is spacious and the worshippers are many? According to al-Shafi'i, yes, and it is said it is a narration from Abu Hanifa. End. He restricted it to the imam being alone, because if some of the congregation stand with the imam, it is said it is disliked, and the correct is that it is not disliked, and this is the custom in the congregational mosques of Muslims in most cities. Thus in al-Muhit. And it is mentioned in al-Bada'i' that whoever considers the meaning of resemblance says it is not disliked, and this is the analogy of al-Tahawi's narration due to the removal of the meaning of resemblance, because the People of the Book do not share the place with the imam. And whoever considers the existence of some corruption says it is disliked, and this is the analogy of the apparent narration due to the existence of some opposition in the place. End. And there is a hidden point. His statement: (and wearing a garment containing images) because it resembles the carrier of an idol, so it is disliked. And in al-Khulasa: And images on a garment are disliked, whether one prays in it or not. End. And these [stray: the place, in, the opposition]. His statement: (and it is mentioned in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli etc.) I say in al-Mi'raj: The text of it: And by our saying al-Shafi'i, may God have mercy on him, said, except if the imam intends to teach the congregation the actions of prayer or the follower intends to convey to the congregation, then it is not disliked according to us. End. His statement: (because if some of the congregation stood) the apparent is that by 'some' is meant a group of the congregation, not one, because in al-Durr al-Mukhtar in the chapter of imamate, that if one stands next to the imam and behind him a row, it is disliked by consensus. His statement: (so it should be forbidden) is a branching from his statement and the apparent of al-Nawawi's speech etc. Then the understood from his context is al-Nawawi's speech and the branching upon it, that his intention is objection to what he transmitted from al-Khulasa, his statement: 'and images on a garment are disliked'. And it can be said: The intention of al-Khulasa is not the depiction of images, but their use, i.e., the use of the garment in which they are, so it equals the author's speech. And it is indicated that this is the intended meaning by the statement of al-Khulasa after his previous expression: 'as for if it is in his hand...'
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, addressing two separate but related rulings within the chapter on what nullifies or is disliked in prayer. The first ruling concerns the imam standing alone on a raised platform (dakkan). The second concerns wearing a garment with images during prayer. The commentary begins by explaining the general dislike of the imam standing in the mihrab (niche) due to resemblance to the People of the Book. The author notes that the mihrab, though part of the mosque, has a form that suggests a separate place, leading to dislike. However, exceptions exist for necessity, such as crowding. A hadith from al-Hakim is cited as proof for the prohibition of the imam standing above the congregation. The commentary then details an intra-Hanafi dispute: the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) holds absolute dislike for the imam on a platform, but al-Tahawi restricts it to the height of a man, and others estimate a cubit. The opposite case—congregation on the platform with the imam below—is also generally disliked, though al-Tahawi reports from the Nawadir that it is not disliked because the cause (resemblance to People of the Book) is absent. The author weighs the positions, favoring the apparent narration for the first ruling, but noting the common practice of shaykhs on the opposite. Exceptions for Friday and Eid prayers due to space are noted, as well as the permissibility if the imam intends to teach. The second ruling on garments with images is simpler: wearing such a garment is disliked because it resembles carrying an idol. Al-Khulasa adds that images on a garment are disliked whether or not one prays in it. The commentary ends with further discussion on the interpretation of al-Khulasa's intention, stating that it refers to using the garment with images, not the act of depiction itself. The passage cuts off mid-sentence during this discussion.

Key Terms
التصاوير (al-tasawir): Images or pictures, specifically on garments. The text discusses dislike of wearing such in prayer.
حامل الصنم (hamil al-sanam): One who carries an idol; the analogy used for garments with images.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text from al-Khulasa, what is the scope of the dislike for images on a garment?
A) It is disliked only if worn during prayer.
B) It is disliked whether one prays in it or not.
C) It is disliked only if the image is of an animate being.
D) It is disliked only if the image is visible to others.

Key Takeaway
Wearing a garment with images is disliked in prayer, and the dislike extends to using such garments even outside prayer.

Salah — Prayer
advanced
12 min
Imam on a Lower Place: Two Hanafi Positions on Karahah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on karahah of imam's height difference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Zahir al-Riwayah and Tahawi positions on the karahah of the imam being lower than the congregation, and identify the legal causes (illa) behind each position.

Core Idea
Imam lower: two causes, one remains; thus karahah persists in Zahir al-Riwayah.

This passage addresses a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: when the congregation stands on a raised platform (dakkan) and the imam is on the ground, is the prayer disliked? The school’s primary transmitted position (Zahir al-Riwayah) says yes, but a narration from al-Tahawi and many later scholars says no. Understanding the reasoning behind each view requires careful analysis of the two causes for karahah: imitation of People of the Book and spatial difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Zahir al-Riwayah position
Identify the ruling from the six core books: both imam higher and imam lower are makruh. Note the two causes: tashabbuh (imitation) and ikhtilaf al-makan (spatial difference).
Zahir al-Riwayah is the primary source of fatwa in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opposing narration
Al-Tahawi narrates from the early Hanafi authorities that only imam higher is makruh; imam lower is not. The basis is that the cause of imitation is absent when the imam is lower.
This narration is from al-Nawadir (rare transmissions).
3
Examine the two causes
Break down the two causes: tashabbuh bi ahl al-kitab and 'some mufsid' (spatial difference). Determine which cause(s) apply when the imam is lower.
Spatial difference exists regardless of who is higher.
4
Analyze the differing views
Scholars who consider only the imitation cause (e.g., Tahawi) say no karahah when imam is lower. Scholars who consider both causes (Zahir al-Riwayah) say karahah remains because spatial difference persists.
Al-Bada'i explains the qiyas (analogy) behind each view.
5
Note the tarjih and exception
The commentator leans toward Zahir al-Riwayah but notes Qadikhan and many mashayikh follow Tahawi. Exception: when there is genuine need (e.g., Jumu'a, 'Eid, teaching), karahah is lifted.
Necessity (hajah) can override the disliked rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الاعتماد، وفي غاية البيان وهو الصحيح، وفي فتح القدير وهو المختار لكن قال: الأوجه الإطلاق وهو ما يقع به الامتياز لأن الموجب وهو شبه الإزدراء يتحقق فيه غير مقتصر على قدر الذراع اهـ. فالحاصل أن التصحيح قد اختلف والأولى العمل بظاهر الرواية وإطلاق الحديث، وأما عكسه وهو انفراد القوم على الدكان بأن يكون الإمام أسفل فهو مكروه أيضاً في ظاهر الرواية وروى الطحاوي عن أصحابنا أنه لا يكره لأن الموجب للكراهة التشبه بأهل الكتاب ولا تشبه هنا لأن مكان إمامهم لا يكون أسفل وجواب ظاهر الرواية أقرب إلى الصواب لأن كراهة كون المكان أرفع كان معلولاً بعلتين : التشبه بأهل الكتاب ووجود بعض المفسد وهو اختلاف المكان وههنا وجدت إحدى العلتين وهي وجود بعض المخالفة. كذا في البدائع. ومن المشايخ من علل الكراهة في الثانية بما في ذلك من شبه الإزدراء بالإمام ولعله أولى، وعلى ما ذكره الطحاوي من عدم الكراهة مشى قاضيخان في فتاواه وعزاه إلى النوادر وقال : وعليه عامة المشايخ .اهـ. وهذا كله عند عدم العذر، أما عند العذر كما في الجمعة والعيدين فإن القوم يقومون على الرفوف والإمام على الأرض ولم يكره ذلك لضيق المكان. كذا في النهاية. وذكر في شرح منية المصلي : وهل يدخل في الحاجة في حق الإمام إرادة تعليم المأمومين أعمال الصلاة وفي حق المأمومين إرادة تبليغ انتقالات الإمام عند اتساع وكثرة المصلين؟ فعند الشافعي نعم قيل وهو رواية عن أبي حنيفة اهـ. قيد بالانفراد لأنه لو قام بعض القوم مع الإمام قيل يكره والأصح أنه لا يكره وبه جرت العادة في جوامع المسلمين في أغلب الأمصار كذا في المحيط. وذكر في البدائع أن من اعتبر معنى التشبه قال لا يكره وهو قياس رواية الطحاوي لزوال معنى التشبه لأن أهل الكتاب لا يشاركون الإمام المكان، ومن اعتبر وجود بعض المفسد قال يكره وهو قياس ظاهر الرواية لوجود بعض في المكان .اهـ. وفيه نظر لا يخفى قوله : (وذكر في شرح منية المصلي (الخ أقول في المعراج ما نصه: وبقولنا قال الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى إلا إذا أراد الإمام تعليم القوم أفعال الصلاة أو أراد المأموم تبليغ القوم فحينئذ لا يكره عندنا اهـ. قوله : (لأنه لو قام بعض القوم الظاهر أن المراد بالبعض جماعة من القوم لا واحد لما في الدر المختار في باب الإمامة من أنه لو قام واحد بجنب الإمام وخلفه صف كره إجماعا
The reliance is on Ghayat al-Bayan and it is the correct view, and in Fath al-Qadir it is the chosen view but he said: the most appropriate is the absolute meaning, which is what establishes distinction because the cause, which is resembling contempt, is realized in it without being limited to a cubit. So the conclusion is that correction has differed, and the better course is to act on the apparent tradition and the generality of the hadith. As for its opposite, i.e., the people being alone on the platform such that the imam is below, it is also disliked in the apparent tradition, and al-Tahawi narrated from our companions that it is not disliked because the cause of dislike is imitation of the People of the Book, and there is no imitation here because their imam's place is not lower. The response of the apparent tradition is closer to correctness because the dislike of the place being higher was caused by two causes: imitation of the People of the Book and the existence of some corruption, which is difference of place, and here one of the two causes is found, which is the existence of some contravention. Thus in al-Bada'i. And some mashayikh gave the cause of dislike in the second case as what is in it of resembling contempt of the imam, and perhaps it is more appropriate. And according to what al-Tahawi mentioned of no dislike, Qadikhan acted in his Fatawa and attributed it to al-Nawadir and said: the majority of mashayikh are upon it. All this is when there is no excuse. As for when there is an excuse, as in Jumu'a and the two 'Ids, the people stand on the shelves and the imam on the ground and that is not disliked due to narrowness of space. Thus in al-Nihaya. And in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli: Does the need include on the part of the imam the desire to teach the followers the actions of prayer, and on the part of the followers the desire to convey the imam's movements when there is ample space and many worshipers? According to al-Shafi'i, yes, and it is said it is a narration from Abu Hanifa. He restricted it to solitude because if some of the people stand with the imam, it is said it is disliked, and the most correct is that it is not disliked, and custom has proceeded upon it in the congregational mosques in most towns. Thus in al-Muhit. And in al-Bada'i it is mentioned that whoever considers the meaning of imitation says it is not disliked, and that is by analogy with Tahawi's narration due to the removal of the meaning of imitation because the People of the Book do not share the place with the imam. And whoever considers the existence of some corruption says it is disliked, and that is by analogy with the apparent tradition due to the existence of some contravention in place. There is consideration in it that is not hidden. His statement: (and it was mentioned in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli etc.) I say in al-Mi'raj: the text is: and by our saying al-Shafi'i said, except if the imam intends to teach the people the actions of prayer or the follower intends to convey to the people, then it is not disliked according to us. His statement: (because if some of the people stood) it is apparent that what is meant by 'some' is a group of people, not one, because in al-Durr al-Mukhtar in the chapter on imamate, that if one person stands beside the imam and behind him a row, it is disliked by consensus.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the ruling when the imam is on a higher place (dakkan) than the congregation, and the reverse when the imam is lower. The primary source (Zahir al-Riwayah) states both cases are disliked (makruh). However, al-Tahawi narrates from Hanafi authorities that only the imam being higher is disliked; when the imam is lower, there is no dislike because the cause (imitation of People of the Book) is absent. The commentator explains that the ruling is based on two causes: tashabbuh (imitation) and existence of some mufsid (spatial difference). When only one cause exists, some scholars rule no karahah. The passage also discusses exceptions: during Jumu'a and 'Eid when space is tight, there is no karahah due to necessity. It also addresses whether the imam's intention to teach the congregation or the congregation's need to see the imam's actions removes the karahah—a view from al-Shafi'i and a narration from Abu Hanifa. Finally, if some of the congregation stand on the same level as the imam, the correct view is no karahah, and this is established practice in large mosques. The passage concludes with a note that the legal cause (illa) is the presence of a contravention in place, and that Tahawi's view (no karahah when imam is lower) is followed by Qadikhan and attributed to al-Nawadir and the majority of mashayikh.

Key Terms
الدكان (al-dakkan): A raised platform or bench on which the imam or congregation stands.
التشبه بأهل الكتاب (al-tashabbuh bi ahl al-kitab): Imitating the practices of Jews and Christians, which is a cause for karahah in prayer arrangements.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The authoritative transmitted position from Imam Muhammad's six books (Zahir al-Riwayah).
النوادر (al-nawadir): Rare or less-transmitted narrations from the early imams, considered weaker than Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the primary reason that the Zahir al-Riwayah holds the imam being lower to be makruh, even though imitation of People of the Book is absent?
A) Because the hadith explicitly forbids it.
B) Because spatial difference (ikhtilaf al-makan) remains as a cause.
C) Because the imam appears to be showing contempt.
D) Because the congregation might not see the imam.

Key Takeaway
When the imam is lower than the congregation, Zahir al-Riwayah rules makruh due to remaining spatial difference, while a strong alternative view from al-Tahawi finds no karahah, a position widely followed in later fatwa.

Ruling on Wearing Clothes with Images in Prayer
Ruling on images during prayer with exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wearing clothes with images of animate beings during prayer, identify when karahah applies, and explain the exceptions when the image is covered or small.

Core Idea
An image of an animate being on clothing during prayer is disliked, but if covered or small, the prayer remains valid.

This passage from Bahra al-Raiq explores the detailed ruling on images (tasawir) during salah. It addresses whether using garments with such images is haram or makruh, and provides exceptions based on visibility and location. We will walk through the evidence and the practical scenarios so that you can apply the ruling correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central dispute
The passage opens with a commentary on whether images on clothes are haram or makruh. Note the different views of al-Nawawi (haram) and al-Khulasa (makruh).
The commentator leans towards haram if the hadith is mutawatir, but the relied-upon position remains makruh.
2
Analyze the evidence (dalil)
The hadith 'Angels do not enter a house in which there is a dog or an image' is cited. Understand how it applies to prayer: by analogy, it indicates prohibition, but the transmission is zanni leading to karahah, not haram.
The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Distinguish between covered and visible images
When the image is covered by another garment or by the hand (e.g., on a ring and not visible), karahah is lifted. The principle is that istitar (covering) removes the dislike.
Examples: ring image covered by clothing, coins in a purse.
4
Examine location-based rulings
Images in front (qibla) are most disliked, then above, behind (disputed). Images on cushions: if upright, disliked; if laid flat, not disliked.
The rulings vary by respect: facing the qibla is greater reverence.
5
Apply the ruling to small images
Small images on coins in a purse are not disliked when covered, but if exposed, karahah applies. The text notes that even small images, if visible, are disliked.
The author in al-Nahr argues that the absence of karahah for small images is not due to covering but because they are small; however, if uncovered, karahah applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فينبغي أن يكون حراماً) تفريع على قوله وظاهر كلام النووي الخ» ثم المتبادر من سياقه كلام النووي والتفريع عليه أن مراده الاعتراض على ما نقله عن الخلاصة من قوله وتكره التصاوير على الثوب الخ» ويمكن أن يقال : ليس مراد الخلاصة تصوير التصاوير بل استعمالها أي استعمال الثوب التي هي فيه فيساوي كلام المصنف، ويدل على أن هذا هو المراد قول الخلاصة بعد عبارته السابقة، أما إذا كان في يده وهو يصلي لا يكره لأنه مستور بثياب، وكذا لو كان على خاتمه . كذا في الخلاصة. وفي المحيط : رجل في يديه تصاوير وهو يؤم الناس لا تكره إمامته لأنها مستورة بالثياب فصار كصورة في نقش خاتم وهو غير مستبين اهـ. وهو يفيد أن المستبين في الخاتم تكره الصلاة معه ويفيد أنه لا يكره أن يصلي ومعه صرة أو كيس فيه دنانير أو دراهم فيها صور صغار لاستتارها، ويفيد أنه لو كان فوق الثوب الذي فيه صورة ثوب ساترله فإنه لا يكره أن يصلي فيه لاستتارها بالثوب الآخر والله سبحانه أعلم . يصور قوله (وأن يكون فوق رأسه أو بين يديه أو بحذائه (صورة) الحديث الصحيحين عنه «لا تدخل الملائكة بيتاً فيه كلب ولا صورة وفي المغرب : الصورة عام في كل ما مشبهاً بخلق الله تعالى من ذوات الروح وغيرها، وقولهم ويكره التصاوير المراد بها التماثيل اهـ. فالحاصل أن الصورة عام والتماثيل خاص والمراد هنا الخاص فإن غير ذي الروح لا يكره كالشجر لما سيأتي والمراد بحذائه يمينه ويساره ولم يذكر ما إذا كانت خلفه للاختلاف، ففي رواية الأصل لا يكره لأنه لا يشبه العبادة، وصرح في الجامع الصغير بالكراهة ومشى عليه في الخلاصة وبأنها إذا كانت في موضع قيامه أو جلوسه لا يكره لأنها استهانة بها، وكذلك على الوسادة إن كانت قائمة يكره لأنه تعظيم لها إن كانت مفروشة لا تكره. كذا في المحيط . قالوا: وأشدها كراهة ما يكون على القبلة أمام المصلي والذي يليه ما يكون فوق رأسه، وهو يصلي لا يكره إلى آخر ما يأتي تأمل قوله : ( ويفيد أنه لا يكره الخ) قال في النهر : غير خاف أن عدم الكراهة في الصغار غني عن التعليل بالاستتار بل مقتضاه ثبوتها إذا كانت منكشفة، وسيأتي أنها لا تكره الصلاة لكن يكره كراهة تنزيه جعل الصورة في البيت لخبر (إن الملائكة لا تدخل بيتاً فيه كلب أو صورة) (۲) .
His statement (it should be haram) is a branch of his statement and the apparent meaning of al-Nawawi's words etc. Then what is understood from his context is al-Nawawi's words and the branch upon it that his intent is to object to what he transmitted from al-Khulasa of his statement 'and images on the garment are disliked' etc. It can be said: what al-Khulasa meant is not the making of images but their use, i.e., the use of the garment in which they are, so it is equal to the wording of the matn. And it is indicated that this is what is meant by the statement of al-Khulasa after his previous statement. As for if it is in his hand while he is praying, it is not disliked because it is covered by his clothes, and similarly if it is on his ring. Thus in al-Khulasa. And in al-Muhit: a man who has images on his hands and he leads people, his imamate is not disliked because they are covered by clothes, so it becomes like an image on the engraving of a ring and it is not visible. This indicates that if the image on the ring is visible, prayer with it is disliked, and it indicates that it is not disliked for him to pray with a purse or pouch containing dinars or dirhams that have small images because they are covered, and it indicates that if there is over the garment that has an image another concealing garment, then it is not disliked to pray in it because the images are concealed by the other garment. And Allah knows best. He makes images. His statement (and that there be above his head or in front of him or beside him an image). The hadith in the two Sahihs: 'Angels do not enter a house in which there is a dog or an image.' And in al-Mughrib: 'image' includes everything that resembles Allah's creation, whether animate or inanimate, and their saying 'images are disliked' means statues. So the result is that 'image' is general and 'statues' is specific, and what is meant here is the specific, for that which is inanimate is not disliked, like trees, as will come. And what is meant by 'beside him' is his right and left. It did not mention if it is behind him due to difference. In the narration of al-Asl, it is not disliked because it does not resemble worship. In al-Jami' al-Saghir, dislike is clearly stated, and al-Khulasa follows it. And if it is in his place of standing or sitting, it is not disliked because it is contempt towards it. Similarly, on a cushion if it is upright, it is disliked because it is glorification, but if it is laid down, it is not disliked. Thus in al-Muhit. They said: the most severely disliked is the one on the qibla in front of the worshipper, and the next is what is above his head. And if he is praying, it is not disliked up to the end of what comes. Consider his statement (and it indicates that it is not disliked etc.). He said in al-Nahr: it is not hidden that the absence of dislike for small images is free from the need for explanation by covering; rather, its implication indicates that dislike applies if they are uncovered. And it will come that it does not dislike prayer but it is disliked as tanzih to put the image in the house due to the report 'Angels do not enter a house in which there is a dog or an image.'
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on having images (tasawir) on clothing or objects during prayer. It begins by questioning whether it is haram or makruh. The commentator cites al-Nawawi's view that depicting animate beings is haram with severe prohibition, and the commentator says if that is the case, it should be haram in prayer as well, not just makruh. However, the Khulasa states that images on a garment are disliked regardless of whether one prays in it or not. The discussion then focuses on practical scenarios: if an image is in the hand (like on a ring) and covered by clothes, there is no karahah. If it is visible, then prayer is disliked. Small images on coins inside a purse are not disliked because they are covered. If a garment with images is worn under another garment that conceals them, there is no karahah. The passage also cites the famous hadith that angels do not enter a house with a dog or an image, but this is about the house, not prayer specifically. It clarifies that the images in question are specifically those of animate beings; images of trees and other inanimate things are not disliked. Regarding the placement of images in the prayer area, the most disliked is an image on the qibla in front of the worshipper, followed by above the head. Images behind the worshipper are not disliked according to some narrations. If an image is on a place where one stands or sits, it is not disliked because it is treated with contempt. Similarly, a pillow or cushion with an image: if it is upright (used for leaning), it is disliked because of glorification; if laid flat (for sitting), it is not disliked. The passage ends by noting that for small images, the absence of karahah is not because they are covered but because they are small, but if exposed, karahah would apply. Finally, it is makruh tanzih to have images in the house at all due to the hadith.

Key Terms
التصاوير (al-tasawir): Images or pictures, specifically of animate beings (animals, humans) that resemble Allah's creation.
التماثيل (al-tamathil): Statues or three-dimensional images, which are the specific type of forbidden images.
مستور (mastur): Covered or concealed; an image that is not visible to others during prayer.
كراهة تنزيه (karahah tanzih): A level of dislike that is not severely prohibited; avoiding it is better but the act is valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling when a person prays with a ring that has an image on it but the image is not visible (ghayr mustabin)?
A) The prayer is invalid (batil).
B) The prayer is valid but makruh.
C) It is not disliked (la yukrah).
D) It is haram to wear such a ring.

Key Takeaway
Wearing clothes with images of animate beings in prayer is makruh tahrimi, but the prayer remains valid; karahah is removed if the image is covered.
