Praying with Images Present: Dislike and Its Exceptions
Details the Hanafi ruling on images in prayer with conditions and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying with images of animate beings, identify the conditions that remove dislike, and distinguish the degrees of dislike based on image placement.

Core Idea
Prayer with an animate image is disliked unless the image is disrespected, covered, or underfoot.

What happens to your prayer if there's a picture of a bird on the wall in front of you? Does it matter if it's a photo or a painting? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the Hanafi position: the presence of an image of an animate being (like a person or animal) in the prayer area triggers dislike (karahah), but the degree depends on location and whether the image is treated with respect or contempt. The ruling is based on a hadith that angels avoid images, yet exceptions exist when the image is 'disrespected' (muhanah) — walked upon or leaned on. This lesson unpacks the evidence, the hierarchy of dislike, and a key internal Hanafi disagreement about images behind the worshipper.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its base ruling
The act being ruled is salah (prayer) performed while an image of an animate being (timthal) is present in certain positions relative to the worshipper. The base ruling according to the Hanafi school is makruh tahrimi (prohibitive dislike).
This ruling does not apply to images of inanimate objects (e.g., trees, mountains) — those are not disliked.
2
Locate the primary proof and its limitation
The hadith 'Angels do not enter a house with a dog or an image' (al-Bukhari, Muslim) is the main dalil. However, the Hanafis limit its application because the hadith itself has exceptions — the Prophet allowed images that are cut into cushions or carpets (case of Aisha's curtain). Thus, the dalil is zanni al-dalala (open to interpretation).
Hanafi usul: the amr (general command) in the hadith is not absolute; mukhassis (specific evidence) restricts it.
3
Analyze the exception for disrespected images
When the image is treated with contempt (muhanah) — for example, it is on a carpet walked upon or a pillow leaned on — the dislike is removed. The proof is the hadith of Jibril and the incident with Aisha's curtain turned into cushions.
The maxim: al-istihsan (juristic preference) overrides the general meaning of the hadith in such cases.
4
Understand the hierarchy of dislike
The text ranks the severity: most disliked is an image on the qiblah wall in front, then above the head, then to the sides, then behind. This hierarchy reflects the degree to which the image resembles an object of worship and diverts attention.
5
Resolve the internal Hanafi dispute about image behind
There is ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school: the original narration (riwayat al-asl) says no dislike for an image behind, while al-Jami' al-Saghir declares it disliked. The mufta bihi (operative opinion) is the latter, because the majority of later scholars (mashayikh) followed it.
The dispute does not affect cases where the image is covered or disrespected — those are agreed upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وأن يكون فوق رأسه أو بين يديه أو بحذائه (صورة) الحديث الصحيحين عنه «لا تدخل الملائكة بيتاً فيه كلب ولا صورة وفي المغرب : الصورة عام في كل ما مشبهاً بخلق الله تعالى من ذوات الروح وغيرها، وقولهم ويكره التصاوير المراد بها التماثيل اهـ. فالحاصل أن الصورة عام والتماثيل خاص والمراد هنا الخاص فإن غير ذي الروح لا يكره كالشجر لما سيأتي والمراد بحذائه يمينه ويساره ولم يذكر ما إذا كانت خلفه للاختلاف، ففي رواية الأصل لا يكره لأنه لا يشبه العبادة، وصرح في الجامع الصغير بالكراهة ومشى عليه في الخلاصة وبأنها إذا كانت في موضع قيامه أو جلوسه لا يكره لأنها استهانة بها، وكذلك على الوسادة إن كانت قائمة يكره لأنه تعظيم لها إن كانت مفروشة لا تكره. كذا في المحيط . قالوا: وأشدها كراهة ما يكون على القبلة أمام المصلي والذي يليه ما يكون فوق رأسه، والذي يليه ما يكون عن يمينه ويساره على الحائط، والذي يليه ما يكون خلفه على الحائط أو الستر. وإنما لم تكره الصلاة في بيت فيه صورة مهانة على بساط يوطأ أو مرفقة يتكأ عليها مع عموم الحديث من أن الملائكة لا تدخله وهو علة الكراهة لأن شر البقاع بقعة لا تدخلها الملائكة لوجود مخصص وهو ما في صحيح ابن حبان: استأذن جبريل عليه السلام على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال : ادخل . فقال : كيف أدخل وفي بيتك ستر فيه تصاوير فإن كنت لا بد فاقطع رؤوسها أو قطعها وسائد أو اجعلها بسطاً. وفي البخاري في كتاب المظالم عن عائشة رضي الله عنها أنها اتخذت على سهوة لها ستراً فيه تماثيل فهتكه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قالت : فاتخذت منه نمرقتين فكانتا في البيت نجلس عليهما، زاد أحمد في مسنده : ولقد رأيته متكئاً على أحدهما وفيه صورة والسهوة كالصفة تكون بين البيت وقيل بيت صغير كالخزانة. والنمرقة بكسر النون وسادة صغيرة والوسادة المخدة لكنه يقتضي عدم كراهة الصلاة على بساط فيه صورة وإن كانت في موضع السجود لأن ذلك ليس بمانع من دخول الملائكة كما أفادته النصوص المخصصة وإن علل بالتشبه بعبادة الأصنام فممنوع فإنهم لا يسجدون عليها وإنما ينصبونها ويتوجهون إليها إلا أن يقال : إن فيها صورة التشبه بعبادتها حال القيام والركوع وفيه تعظيم لها إن سجد عليها، ولهذا أطلق الكراهة في الأصل فيما إذا كان على البساط المصلى عليه صورة لأن الذي يصلي عليه معظم فوضع الصورة فيه تعظيم لها بخلاف البساط الذي ليس بمصلى، وتقدم عن الجامع الصغير التقييد بموضع السجود فينبغي أن يحمل إطلاق الأصل عليه، وإنها إذا كانت تحت قدميه لا يكره اتفاقاً. وفي الخلاصة: ولا بأس بأن يصلي على بساط فيه تصاوير لكن لا يسجد عليها ثم قال : ثم التمثال إن كان على وسادة أو بساط لا بأس باستعمالهما وإن كان يكره اتخاذهما . ثم اعلم أن العلماء اختلفوا فيما إذا كانت [النص ينقطع هنا]
His statement: 'And that above his head, or in front of him, or opposite him be an image' [from the matn]. The hadith in the two Sahihs: 'Angels do not enter a house in which there is a dog or an image.' And in al-Mughrib: 'Image (surah) is general for everything that resembles the creation of Allah, whether it has a soul or not. And their statement, 'It is disliked to make images,' means statues (tamathil).' End quote. So the conclusion is that 'surah' is general and 'tamathil' is specific, and what is intended here is the specific, for that which has no soul is not disliked, like a tree, as will come. And 'opposite him' means his right and left. He did not mention if it is behind him due to difference of opinion: according to one narration, it is not disliked because it does not resemble worship, but in al-Jami' al-Saghir, he explicitly stated dislike, and al-Khulasa followed that. And if the image is at his standing or sitting place, it is not disliked because it is a form of disrespect. Similarly, on a cushion, if it is upright, it is disliked because it honors it; if it is flat (mufarrashah), it is not disliked. Thus in al-Muhit. They said: The most severely disliked is that which is on the qiblah in front of the worshipper, then that which is above his head, then that which is on his right and left on the wall, then that which is behind him on the wall or curtain. And prayer in a house containing an image that is disrespected (muhanah) on a carpet that is walked upon or a cushion that is leaned on is not disliked, despite the general meaning of the hadith that angels do not enter (and this is the cause of dislike), because the worst of places is a place where angels do not enter due to the existence of a specific evidence (mukhassis). And that is what is in Sahih Ibn Hibban: 'Jibril asked permission to enter upon the Prophet, and he said: How can I enter while in your house there is a curtain with images? If you must, then cut off their heads or turn them into cushions or make them into carpets.' And in al-Bukhari in the Book of Oppressions from Aisha that she took a curtain with figures, and the Prophet tore it; she said: Then I made two pillows (namiraqat) from it, and they were in the house and we sat on them. Ahmad added: And I saw him leaning on one of them and there was an image on it. 'Al-sahwah' is like a canopy between the houses, or a small room like a closet. 'Al-namiqah' (with kasra) is a small cushion, and 'al-wisadah' is a pillow. But this indicates the absence of dislike for praying on a carpet that has an image, even if it is at the place of prostration, because that does not prevent the entry of angels, as the specific evidences show. And if it is explained by resemblance to idol worship, it is rejected because they do not prostrate on them, but rather set them up and face them. Except that it can be said that it contains a form of resemblance to worship during standing and bowing, and it involves honor if one prostrates on it. For this reason, the original text (al-asl) declared dislike when the image is on the prayer mat itself, because the one praying on it is honoring it; placing an image on it is a form of honor. This is unlike a mat that is not used for prayer. The restriction to the place of prostration came from al-Jami' al-Saghir, so the absolute statement of the original should be understood as applying to that. And if it is under his feet, it is not disliked by agreement. And in al-Khulasa: There is no harm in praying on a carpet with images as long as one does not prostrate on them. Then he said: If the statue is on a cushion or carpet, there is no harm in using them, although it is disliked to acquire them. Then know that the scholars differed regarding when... [text cuts off]
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling with proof on the Hanafi position regarding praying with images present. It addresses the hadith that angels do not enter a house with a dog or image, which is the primary proof for dislike. The commentator explains that 'surah' (image) in the hadith is general, but the ruling applies only to images of animate beings (tamathil); images of inanimate objects (like trees) are not disliked. The passage then specifies the degrees of dislike based on the image's location: most severe is on the qiblah in front, then above the head, then to the sides, then behind. Prayer is not disliked if the image is disrespected (e.g., on a carpet walked upon or a cushion leaned on), due to the practice of the Prophet with Aisha's curtain. The key principle is that if the image is covered, small, headless, or treated with disrespect (muhanah), the dislike is removed. There is a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school: according to one narration, images behind the worshipper are not disliked, but al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Khulasa declare it disliked. The text also discusses whether the dislike is due to preventing angels or resembling idol worship; the preferred view is the former. This passage shows the careful balancing of textual evidence (hadith) and practical considerations (custom, disrespect) in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
صورة (surah): Image; in this context, specifically images of animate beings (tamathil), as opposed to inanimate objects.
تمثال (timthal): Statue or three-dimensional figure; in this context, it refers to any representation of an animate being.
مهانة (muhanah): Disrespected, treated with contempt; images that are walked upon or leaned on are considered muhanah and do not cause dislike.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following scenarios makes prayer most severely disliked?
A) An image on a cushion that is leaned on.
B) An image on the qiblah wall in front of the worshipper.
C) An image on a carpet that is walked upon.
D) An image on a ring covered by clothing.

Key Takeaway
Prayer with an animate image is makruh tahrimi, but this dislike is lifted if the image is disrespected (muhanah), covered, or underfoot; the severity varies by location, with the front being worst.

Ruling on Counting Ayat and Tasbih During Prayer
Explains the disliked nature of counting verses and tasbih in prayer and the intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on counting verses/tasbih in prayer and identify the intra-madhhab difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Counting with the hand during prayer is makruh according to Zahir al-Riwayah, but the Sahibayn allowed it in ghayr al-Riwayah.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains when counting verses or tasbih during prayer is disliked and why. It also presents a valid difference of opinion within the Hanafi school, requiring us to distinguish between the authoritative Zahir al-Riwayah and the less relied-upon ghayr al-Riwayah narrations. Understanding this distinction is key to applying the correct fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? (Counting verses/tasbih during prayer). What is the hukm in Zahir al-Riwayah?
The ruling is makruh (disliked) according to the majority.
2
Note the intra-madhhab dispute
Who differs? (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). What is their view and on what basis?
They consider it permissible in ghayr al-Riwayah.
3
Examine the restrictions
What limitations are mentioned? (Counting with hand vs. finger tips, tongue, outside prayer, etc.)
The dispute is restricted to physical counting (hand/fingers/thread). Other methods are agreed upon.
4
Review the dalil
What evidence is cited? (Hadith of women counting tasbih on fingertips, hadith of Sa'd). How does the author use it?
The Prophet did not forbid counting with stones, indicating permissibility outside prayer.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Which position is relied upon for fatwa? (Zahir al-Riwayah). Why?
Because it is the authoritative layer of transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وعد الآي (والتسبيح أي ويكره عد الآيات من القرآن والتسبيح وكذا السور لأنه ليس من أعمال الصلاة أطلقه فشمل العد في الفرائض والنوافل جميعاً باتفاق أصحابنا في ظاهر الرواية، وروي عنهما في غير ظاهر الرواية أن العد باليد لا بأس به، كذا العناية وغيرها لكن في الكافي وقالا لا بأس به فجزم به عنهما وعلل لهما بأن المصلي يضطر إلى ذلك لمراعاة سنة القراءة والعمل بما جاءت به السنة في صلاة السبيح، وقال عليه السلام لنسوة سألنه عن التسبيح : أعددنه بالأنامل فإنهن مسؤولات مستنطقات يوم القيامة . وقوله في الهداية قلنا يمكنه أن يعد ذلك قبل الشروع إنما يأتي هذا في الآي دون التسبيحات ا هـ. قالوا: ومحل الاختلاف هو العد باليد كما وقع التقييد به في الهداية، سواء كان بأصابعه أو بخيط يمسكه، أما الغمز برؤوس الأصابع أو الحفظ بالقلب فهو غير مكروه اتفاقاً والعد باللسان مفسد اتفاقاً. وقيد بالآي والتسبيح لأن عد الناس وغيرهم مكروه اتفاقاً. كذا في غاية البيان. وقيد بالصلاة لأنا لعد خارج الصلاة لا يكره على الصحيح كما ذكره المصنف في المستصفي لأنه أسكن للقلب وأجلب للنشاط ولما رواه أبو داود والترمذي والنسائي وابن حبان والحاكم قال سعد بن أبي وقاص أنه دخل مع النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم على امرأة وبين يديها نوى أو حصى تسج به فقال : أخبرك بما هو أيسر عليك من هذا أو أفضل فقال : سبحان الله عدد ما خلق في السماء، وسبحان الله عدد ما خلق في الأرض، وسبحان الله عدد ما ذلك، وسبحان الله عدد ما هو خالق والحمد لله مثل ذلك، والله أكبر مثل بين ذلك، ولا إله إلا الله مثل ذلك، ولا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله مثل ذلك. فلم ينهها عن ذلك
His statement: (and counting of verses and tasbih) meaning: it is disliked to count verses of the Quran and tasbih, and likewise surahs, because it is not from the actions of prayer. He applied it generally, so it includes counting in obligatory and supererogatory prayers, by agreement of our companions in zahir al-riwayah. And it is narrated from them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) in ghayr zahir al-riwayah that counting with the hand is not objectionable. Thus in al-‘Inayah and others. But in al-Kafi: they said there is no harm in it, so it is affirmed from them. They reasoned that the worshiper is compelled to that to observe the sunnah of recitation and to act upon what the sunnah brought in Salat al-Tasbih. And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said to some women who asked him about tasbih: 'Count them with the fingertips, for they will be questioned and made to speak on the Day of Resurrection.' And his statement in al-Hidayah: we said it is possible for him to count that before starting. This applies to verses, not to tasbih. End. They said: the point of difference is counting with the hand, as restricted in al-Hidayah, whether with his fingers or with a thread he holds. As for pressing with the tips of the fingers or memorizing with the heart, it is not disliked by agreement. And counting with the tongue invalidates the prayer by agreement. It is restricted to verses and tasbih because counting people and others is disliked by agreement. Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan. And it is restricted to prayer because counting outside prayer is not disliked according to the sound opinion, as the author mentioned in al-Mustasfa, because it is more calming for the heart and more conducive to activity. And due to what Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa’i, Ibn Hibban, and al-Hakim narrated: Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas said that he entered with the Prophet (peace be upon him) upon a woman, and in front of her were date pits or pebbles with which she was making tasbih. He said: 'Shall I inform you of what is easier for you than this, or better?' Then he said: 'Subhan Allah the number of what He created in the heavens, Subhan Allah the number of what He created on the earth, Subhan Allah the number of what is between that, Subhan Allah the number of what He is going to create, and al-Hamdulillah likewise, and Allahu Akbar likewise, and La ilaha illa Allah likewise, and La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah likewise.' And he did not forbid her from that.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling of counting verses and tasbih during prayer. The commentator begins by stating that it is disliked (makruh) to count verses of the Quran, tasbih, and surahs while in prayer, because such counting is not part of the actions of prayer. This ruling applies to both obligatory and supererogatory prayers, according to the agreement of the Hanafi school in Zahir al-Riwayah. However, there is a narration from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) outside Zahir al-Riwayah that counting with the hand is not objectionable. Some sources, like al-Kafi, affirm this view from them, reasoning that a worshiper may need to count to observe the sunnah of recitation, as in Salat al-Tasbih. The Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed women to count tasbih on their fingertips. The difference of opinion is specifically about counting with the hand (by fingers or a thread). Pressing finger tips or mental counting is not disliked by consensus. Counting with the tongue invalidates the prayer by consensus. The restriction to verses and tasbih means counting people or other things is disliked by agreement. Counting outside prayer is not disliked on the sound view, supported by the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, where the Prophet taught a superior form of dhikr but did not forbid the woman from using stones.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that form the authoritative foundation of the Hanafi school.
عد الآي (‘add al-ayi): Counting the verses of the Quran during prayer, either to ensure correct recitation or for other purposes.
العد باليد (al-‘add bil-yad): Counting by using the fingers or a thread held in the hand.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on counting verses with the hand during prayer?
A) It is permissible without dislike.
B) It is disliked (makruh).
C) It invalidates the prayer.
D) It is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
Counting verses or tasbih with the hand during prayer is disliked (makruh) in the relied-upon Hanafi position, though the Sahibayn permitted it in non-standard narrations.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Ruling on Using the Subha (Rosary) and Salat al-Tasbih
Defends permissibility of subha and describes Salat al-Tasbih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using a subha for dhikr and describe the method and virtue of Salat al-Tasbih, citing the primary evidence.

Core Idea
The subha is permissible and Salat al-Tasbih is a sunnah with immense reward, both rooted in authentic hadith.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses two practices often questioned by Muslims: using prayer beads (subha) and the specific prayer known as Salat al-Tasbih. The commentator defends both against claims of innovation, providing evidence from the Prophet's practice and the approval of early Muslims. You will learn the legal rulings and the reasoning behind them, enabling you to distinguish between permissible tools and religious innovations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two practices and their rulings
First, isolate the two practices: (1) using a subha to count dhikr, and (2) performing Salat al-Tasbih. Note that the Hanafi school considers both to be permissible (mubah) and recommended (sunnah), respectively.
2
Locate the primary proofs
For the subha, the proof is the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas (referenced in the commentary) where the Prophet did not forbid a woman from counting on stones. For Salat al-Tasbih, the proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas teaching the prayer to al-Abbas.
Both hadiths are ahad, thus zanni al-thubut, but they are considered reliable by the Hanafi scholars.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal implication)
The Prophet's approval of counting stones implies that using any means for counting, including a string of beads, is permissible. For Salat al-Tasbih, the explicit instruction from the Prophet to pray four rak'ahs with specific tasbih indicates its recommendation and virtue.
4
Note the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf on counting with the hand in prayer
Some Hanafi scholars (al-Halabi) consider counting with the hand in prayer as tanzihi (disliked), while others (al-Nihaya) deem it tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). The commentator resolves that the mufta bihi is tanzihi, and the permissibility of subha outside prayer remains unaffected.
The subha is used outside prayer; counting with the hand inside prayer is a separate issue.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
The commentator relies on the works of al-Ramli and Ibn Hajar al-Haytami, who affirm the subha's basis in the sunnah. For Salat al-Tasbih, the hadith of Ibn Abbas is accepted, and the prayer is considered a highly meritorious nafilah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ثم هذا الحديث ونحوه مما يشهد الخ) قال الرملي : والظاهر أنها ليست ببدعة فقد قال ابن حجر الهيتمي في شرح الأربعين النواوية : السبحة ورد لها أصل أصيل عن بعض أمهات المؤمنين وأقرها النبي على ذلك قوله : (وظاهر النهاية أنها تحريمية الخ) قال في النهر : فيه نظر إذ المكروه تنزيهاً غير مباح أي غير مستوي الطرفين .اهـ. قال الرملي : الغالب إطلاقهم غير المباح على المحرم أو المكروه تحريماً وإن كان يطلق على ما ذكر . فلا جرم وإنما أرشدها إلى ما هو أيسر وأفضل ولو كان مكروهاً لبين لها ذلك. ثم هذا الحديث ونحوه مما يشهد بأنه لا بأس باتخاذ السبحة المعروفة لإحصاء عدد الأذكار إذ لا تزيد السبحة على مضمون هذا الحديث إلا بضم النوى ونحوه في خيط، ومثل هذا لا يظهر تأثيره في المنع أن نقل اتخاذها والعمل بها عن جماعة من الصوفية الأخيار وغيرهم اللهم إلا إذا ترتب عليها رياء وسمعة فلا كلام لنا فيه . وهذا الحديث أيضاً يشهد لأفضلية هذا الذكر المخصوص على ذكر مجرد عن هذه الصيغة ولو تكرر يسيراً. ثم اعلم أن العلامة الحلبي ذكر أن كراهة العد باليد في الصلاة تنزيهية وظاهر النهاية أنها تحريمية فإنه قال : والصحيح أنه لا يباح العد أصلاً لأنه ليس في الكتاب فصل بين الفرض والنفل وقد يصير العد عملاً كثيراً فيوجب فساد الصلاة وما روي في الأحاديث من قرأ في الصلاة كذا وكذا مرة قل هو أحد وكذا كذا تسبيحة فتلك الأحاديث لم يصححها الثقات، أما صلاة التسبيح فقد أوردها وهي صلاة مباركة فيها ثواب عظيم ومنافع كثيرة فإنه يقدر أن يحفظ بالقلب وإن احتاج يعد بالأنامل حتى لا يصير عملاً كثيراً ! ثم صلاة التسبيح هذه ما رواها عكرمة عن ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم للعباس بن عبد المطلب يا عباس يا عماه إلا أعطيك ألا أمنحك ألا أحبوك ألا أفعل بك عشر خصال إذا أنت فعلت ذلك غفر الله لك ذنبك أوله وآخره، قديمه وحديثه خطأه ،وعمده صغيره وكبيره سره وعلانيته. عشر خصال أن تصلي أربع ركعات تقرأ في كل ركعة بفاتحة الكتاب وسورة فإذا فرغت من القراءة في أول ركعة فقل وأنت قائم سبحان الله والحمد الله ولا إله إلا الله والله أكبر خمس عشرة مرة، ثم تركع فتقول وأنت راكع عشراً، ثم ترفع رأسك من الركوع فتقولها عشراً، ثم تهوي ساجداً فتقولها وأنت ساجد عشراً، ثم ترفع رأسك من السجود فتقولها عشراً، ثم تسجد الثانية فتقولها عشراً، ثم ترفع رأسك من السجود فتقولها عشراً فذلك خمس وسبعون في كل ركعة تفعل ذلك في أربع ركعات إن استطعت أن تصليها في كل يوم مرة فافعل، فإن لم تستطع ففي كل جمعة مرة، فإن لم تفعل ففي كل شهر مرة فإن لم تفعل ففي كل سنة مرة، فإن لم قوله : (ثم صلاة التسبيح الخ) اقتصر المؤلف على هذه الرواية في الحاوي القدسي، وثم رواية أخرى أوردها الترمذي في جامعه عبد الله بن المبارك وقد ذكر الروايتين الحلبي في شرح المنية واقتصر على الثانية في القنية فقال في حديثها : رواه أبو عيسى في جامعه وعبد الله بن أبي حفص في جامعه وحميد بن زنجويه في الترغيب بروايتين، والمختار منهما أن يكبر ويقرأ سبحانك اللهم الخ. ثم يقول سبحان الله والحمد لله ولا إله إلا الله والله أكبر خمس عشرة مرة، ثم يقرأ الفاتحة وسورة مثل سورة «والضحى ثم يقول سبحان الله الخ . عشر مرات ثم يركع ويقول سبحان, العظيم ثلاثاً ثم يقول سبحان الله عشراً، ثم يرفع رأسه ويقول سمع الله لمن حمده ربنا لك الحمد ويقول سبحان الله الخ عشر مرات، ثم يكبر ويسجد ويسبح ثلاثاً ثم يقول سبحان الله الخ عشراً،
His statement: (Then this hadith and its like testify...) al-Ramli said: The apparent view is that it is not a bid'ah. Ibn Hajar al-Haytami said in his commentary on al-Arba'in al-Nawawiyya: The subha has a genuine basis from some of the Mothers of the Believers, and the Prophet approved it. His statement: (And the apparent meaning of al-Nihaya is that it is prohibitively disliked...) He said in al-Nahr: There is consideration in this, for the tanzihi dislike is not permissible, meaning not equal in its two sides. End. Al-Ramli said: Generally their usage of 'non-permissible' refers to the forbidden or prohibitively disliked, even if it is applied to what was mentioned. So no wonder, and he guided her to what is easier and better, and if it had been disliked he would have explained that to her. Then this hadith and its like testify that there is no harm in using the well-known subha (rosary) for counting the number of dhikr, for the subha adds nothing to the content of this hadith except stringing the stones on a thread. Such a thing does not appear to have an effect in prohibition; indeed, its use and practice is transmitted from a group of the righteous Sufis and others, except if it leads to ostentation and reputation, then we have no word on it. This hadith also testifies to the superiority of this specific dhikr over a dhikr devoid of this formula, even if repeated slightly. Then know that al-Allamah al-Halabi mentioned that the dislike of counting with the hand in prayer is tanzihi, and the apparent view of al-Nihaya is that it is tahrimi. He said: The correct view is that it is not permissible at all because there is no distinction in the Book between obligatory and supererogatory, and counting may become excessive action causing invalidation of prayer. As for the hadiths about reading in prayer such and such number of times 'Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad' and such and such tasbih, those hadiths are not authenticated by the trustworthy. As for Salat al-Tasbih, he presented it, and it is a blessed prayer with great reward and many benefits. One can memorize in the heart, and if needed, count with the fingertips so that it does not become excessive action. Then this Salat al-Tasbih was narrated by 'Ikrimah from Ibn 'Abbas who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said to al-'Abbas ibn 'Abd al-Muttalib: 'O 'Abbas, O my uncle, shall I not give you, shall I not grant you, shall I not bestow upon you, shall I not do for you ten characteristics? If you do them, Allah will forgive your sins, first and last, old and new, error and intention, small and great, secret and public. The ten characteristics are: You pray four rak'ahs, reciting in each rak'ah al-Fatihah and a surah. When you finish recitation in the first rak'ah, while standing say: Subhan Allah, wa al-Hamdu lillah, wa la ilaha illa Allah, wa Allahu Akbar fifteen times. Then bow and say it while bowing ten times. Then raise your head from bowing and say it ten times. Then prostrate and say it while prostrating ten times. Then raise your head from prostration and say it ten times. Then prostrate a second time and say it ten times. Then raise your head from prostration and say it ten times. That is seventy-five in each rak'ah. Do that in four rak'ahs. If you can pray it once every day, do so. If not, once every week. If not, once every month. If not, once every year. If not...' His statement: (Then Salat al-Tasbih) The author restricted to this narration in al-Hawi al-Qudsi. There is another narration transmitted by al-Tirmidhi in his Jami' from 'Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak. Al-Halabi mentioned both narrations in his commentary on al-Munyah and restricted to the second in al-Qunyah. He said in its hadith: It was narrated by Abu 'Isa in his Jami', 'Abdullah ibn Abi Hafs in his Jami', and Humaid ibn Zanjawayh in al-Targhib in two versions. The chosen of them is that he says the takbir and recites 'Subhanaka Allahumma...' then says Subhan Allah, al-Hamdu lillah, la ilaha illa Allah, Allahu Akbar fifteen times, then recites al-Fatihah and a surah like 'Wa al-Duha', then says Subhan Allah... ten times, then bows and says Subhan al-'Azim three times, then says Subhan Allah ten times, then raises his head and says Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, Rabbana laka al-hamd, and says Subhan Allah... ten times, then says takbir and prostrates and says Subhan three times, then says Subhan Allah... ten times.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage addresses two related topics: the permissibility of using a subha (rosary or beads) for counting dhikr, and the method and virtue of Salat al-Tasbih. The commentary begins by discussing the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas (previously cited), emphasizing that the Prophet did not forbid the woman from using stones to count dhikr. Al-Ramli and Ibn Hajar al-Haytami affirm that the subha has a basis in the sunnah (from some of the Prophet's wives and his approval). The subha is simply a string of beads, and there is no inherent prohibition; however, if it leads to ostentation, it becomes problematic. The passage then clarifies that counting with the hand in prayer is a separate issue (mainly tanzihi dislike, although some say tahrimi). The focus shifts to Salat al-Tasbih, a prayer taught by the Prophet to his uncle al-'Abbas. It consists of four rak'ahs with a specific sequence of tasbih (75 per rak'ah). The prayer is highly meritorious, promising forgiveness of sins. The text provides the method according to the narration of Ibn 'Abbas, and then mentions a second narration from al-Tirmidhi with slight variations. The commentator notes that the author of the matn (likely al-Hidayah) relied on the first narration, but the second is also accepted. The prayer is considered a blessed, non-obligatory act of worship that can be performed daily, weekly, monthly, or yearly depending on one's capacity.

Key Terms
السبحة (al-subha): A string of beads used for counting the number of dhikr (e.g., tasbih, tahmid, takbir).
صلاة التسبيح (salat al-tasbih): A supererogatory prayer consisting of four rak'ahs with 75 tasbih in each rak'ah, taught by the Prophet to his uncle al-'Abbas.
بدعة (bid'ah): An innovation in religion, which is generally considered prohibited; the text argues that the subha and Salat al-Tasbih are not bid'ah because they have a basis.
تنزيهي (tanzihi): Lightly disliked; an act whose avoidance is recommended but not sinful.
تحريمي (tahrimi): Prohibitively disliked; an act closer to haram but not conclusively forbidden.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on using a subha (rosary) for counting dhikr?
A) It is a prohibited innovation.
B) It is permissible and has a basis in the sunnah.
C) It is makruh tahrimi.
D) It is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
The subha is a permissible tool for dhikr, and Salat al-Tasbih is a sunnah prayer of immense merit, both supported by authentic practice and scholarly consensus within the Hanafi school.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Counting Tasbih and the Method of Salat al-Tasbih
Expands ruling on counting tasbih and details Salat al-Tasbih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on counting tasbih during prayer, distinguish between the tanzihi and tahrimi views, and explain the method and virtue of Salat al-Tasbih as reported in the hadith.

Core Idea
Counting tasbih in prayer is disliked, but Salat al-Tasbih is a meritorious prayer with a specific tasbih formula.

This lesson examines the nuanced Hanafi ruling on counting tasbih (glorifications) during prayer, a matter where two views exist within the school: tanzihi (lightly disliked) and tahrimi (prohibitively disliked). We will also explore the special prayer called Salat al-Tasbih, its hadith-based method, and its abundant reward. By understanding the proofs and distinctions, you will be able to apply the correct ruling and appreciate the school's balanced approach.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the intra-Hanafi dispute
Recognize that the act in question is counting tasbih during prayer using fingers or a subha. The Hanafi school has differing views: al-Halabi says it is makruh tanzihi, while al-Nihayah says it is makruh tahrimi.
Also note that using subha outside prayer is not an issue.
2
Analyze the evidence for each position
The hadith of Salat al-Tasbih (from Ikrima) is cited as evidence for permissibility when done without excess. The opposing view relies on the principle that any unnecessary action may invalidate prayer and that hadiths on counting are weak.
The text notes that the hadith is authentic and supported by practice of righteous people.
3
Determine the relied-upon position (mufta bihi)
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq favors the tanzihi view, indicating that counting is makruh tanzihi, not tahrimi. The mufta bihi is that it is lightly disliked; if necessary, one may count by gesture.
This has practical implications: if tahrimi, it would be sinful and may invalidate if excessive.
4
Study the method of Salat al-Tasbih
Two narrations are given: one from al-Hawi al-Qudsi (the first) and another from Ibn al-Mubarak (the second). The second is preferred in al-Qunya because it avoids the jalsat al-istiraha, which is disliked in the Hanafi school.
Both methods involve 300 tasbihs per four rak'ats with specific distribution.
5
Understand the exception: counting by gesture in necessity
If one needs to count, he should do so by gesture (ishara) without pronouncing. This is allowed only in cases of necessity (idhtirar).
This applies to Salat al-Tasbih and any other prayer where counting is needed.

Source Text

As for the hadiths that say 'whoever recites in prayer such and such times Qul Huwa Ahad and such and such tasbihs', those hadiths were not authenticated by trustworthy narrators. As for Salat al-Tasbih, it has been reported and it is a blessed prayer with great reward and many benefits, for one can memorize by heart, and if he needs to count with his fingers... then this Salat al-Tasbih was narrated by Ikrima from Ibn Abbas who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said to al-Abbas ibn Abd al-Muttalib: O Abbas, O uncle, shall I give you, shall I grant you, shall I love you, shall I do for you ten deeds? If you do them, Allah will forgive your sins, first and last, old and new, error and intention, small and great, secret and public. Ten deeds: you pray four rak'ats, reciting in each rak'at al-Fatiha and a sura, and when you finish recitation in the first rak'at, while standing, say 'Subhan Allah, al-Hamdulillah, La ilaha illa Allah, Allahu Akbar' fifteen times, then bow and say it ten times while bowing, then raise your head from bowing and say it ten times, then prostrate and say it ten times while prostrating, then raise your head from prostration and say it ten times, then prostrate a second time and say it ten times, then raise your head from prostration and say it ten times; that totals seventy-five in each rak'at. Do that in four rak'ats. If you can pray it once daily, do so; if not, once every Friday; if not, once every month; if not, once every year; if not, once in your lifetime. Narrated by Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, and al-Tabarani, and he said at the end: 'Even if your sins were like the foam of the sea or the sand of the desert, Allah would forgive you.' Al-Hafiz Abd al-Azim al-Mundhiri said: This hadith has been narrated through many chains from a group of companions, and the best is this hadith of Ikrima, and a group declared it authentic. Fakhr al-Islam mentioned in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir: Our shaykhs said: If one needs to count, he should count by gesture without pronouncing, and his actions are valid in the case of necessity. End quote. In his statement: 'Then Salat al-Tasbih etc.' The author confined to this narration in al-Hawi al-Qudsi. There is another narration reported by al-Tirmidhi in his Jami' from Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak. Al-Halabi mentioned both narrations in Sharh al-Munya and confined to the second in al-Qunya, saying in its hadith: It was narrated by Abu Isa in his Jami', Abdullah ibn Abi Hafs in his Jami', and Humayd ibn Zanjawayh in al-Targhib in two versions. The chosen one is that he says takbir and recites 'Subhanaka Allahumma...', then says 'Subhan Allah, al-Hamdulillah, La ilaha illa Allah, Allahu Akbar' fifteen times, then recites al-Fatiha and a sura like al-Duha, then says 'Subhan Allah...' ten times, then bows and says 'Subhan Rabbi al-Azim' three times, then says 'Subhan Allah...' ten times, then raises his head and says 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, Rabbana laka al-hamd' and says 'Subhan Allah...' ten times, then says takbir and prostrates and glorifies three times, then says 'Subhan Allah...' ten times, then raises his head and says takbir and sits, then says 'Subhan Allah...' ten times, then says takbir and prostrates and glorifies three times, then says 'Subhan Allah...' ten times, then stands and does the same in the second rak'at. He prays four rak'ats with one salutation and two sittings. End quote. In Sharh al-Munya, Ibn al-Mubarak was asked: If one forgets in this prayer, should he say the tasbihs in the prostration of forgetfulness ten each? He said: It is only three hundred tasbihs. End quote. This description mentioned by Ibn al-Mubarak is the one mentioned in Mukhtasar al-Bahr, and it accords with our school because there is no need for the sitting of rest (jalsat al-istiraha), which is disliked according to us, as previously mentioned in its place. End quote. This was the reason for the author of al-Qunya to choose this method, but since the other method is also established from him, it is not...
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding disliked actions in prayer. The author addresses the ruling of counting tasbih (glorifications) using fingers or prayer beads (subha) during prayer. He begins by citing a hadith that indicates there is no harm in using a prayer bead string (subha) for counting dhikr, as it is merely an aid. However, he then presents a dispute between al-Allama al-Halabi and the author of al-Nihayah. Al-Halabi considers counting with the hand in prayer to be makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked), while al-Nihayah holds it is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) and even risks invalidating the prayer if it becomes excessive action. The passage then defends the authenticity and virtue of Salat al-Tasbih, a special prayer involving numerous tasbihs, by quoting a hadith from Ikrima via Ibn Abbas. Two narrations of the method are given: one from al-Hawi al-Qudsi (the first) and another from al-Tirmidhi via Ibn al-Mubarak (the second, preferred by the author of al-Qunya). The discussion concludes that if one needs to count in prayer, he should do so by gesture (ishara) without pronouncing, and that this applies only in cases of necessity. The commentator also notes that the method of Ibn al-Mubarak (the second narration) is consistent with the Hanafi school's dislike of the sitting of rest (jalsat al-istiraha). The overall ruling: counting tasbih in prayer is disliked (karahah), with a difference of opinion on the degree; the relied-upon position is that it is makruh tanzihi. Using a subha is not prohibited as long as it does not lead to show-off.

Key Terms
السبحة (al-subha): A string of beads used to count tasbih, dhikr, etc.
العد باليد (al-‘addu bil-yad): Counting using fingers or hand gestures to keep track of repetitions.
صلاة التسبيح (salat al-tasbih): A special supererogatory prayer of four rak'ats with many tasbihs, reported in hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Killing Snakes and Scorpions During Prayer: Permissibility and Precaution
Ruling on killing snakes and scorpions while praying

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing snakes and scorpions during prayer and distinguish when caution is required due to the possibility of jinn.

Core Idea
Killing snakes and scorpions in prayer is allowed by hadith, but white snakes may be jinn and should be spared.

The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states that killing a snake or scorpion is not disliked during prayer. The commentary in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq brings the primary evidence from the Sahihain: the command 'Kill the two black ones in prayer: the snake and the scorpion.' However, a further nuance arises from a caution in al-Muhit about white snakes possibly being jinn. This lesson unpacks the proof, the intra-Hanafi disagreement, and the operative ruling (mufta bihi).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling from the matn
The matn (base text) of Kanz al-Daqa'iq says 'لا قتل الحية والعقرب', meaning it is not disliked (makruh) to kill a snake or scorpion during prayer. This implies permissibility (ibaha) or even recommendation for the scorpion.
The ruling is about permissibility within prayer, not about whether the act of killing is itself permissible outside prayer.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The commentary cites the hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim: 'اقتلوا الأسودين في الصلاة الحية والعقرب' (Kill the two black ones in prayer: the snake and the scorpion). This is the primary proof.
The hadith is mutawatir in meaning (thubut = qati) and clear in indication (dalala = qati).
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof indicates the ruling)
In Hanafi usul, the imperative 'اقتلوا' (kill) indicates permissibility (ibaha) as the minimum level, unless there is a qarina (contextual indicator) making it obligatory. No such qarina exists here; thus the action is mubah, and for scorpions it is mustahabb due to the specific recommendation in other narrations.
The Hanafi position: al-amr yufidu al-ibaha, not wujub, unless there is evidence of obligation.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf about white snakes
Al-Muhit reports a view that the white snake should not be killed because it could be a jinn, citing the hadith 'إياكم والحية البيضاء فإنها من الجن'. Al-Tahawi disagrees, permitting killing all snakes based on the general covenant. The preferred view (al-ula) is to warn the snake first (outside prayer) and only kill if it persists.
This ikhtilaf adds a layer of caution: in prayer, if one suspects a snake is a jinn, it is better to avoid killing if possible, but if killed, the prayer remains valid.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position: It is permissible to kill snakes and scorpions in prayer; for scorpions it is mustahabb. However, if there is suspicion that a snake is a jinn, one should try to warn it (outside prayer) and avoid killing it inside prayer if possible. The prayer is not invalidated by the killing.
This ruling reflects the later Hanafi authorities (fatawa mutakhkhirin) who emphasize caution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لا قتل الحية والعقرب أي لا يكره قتلهما لحديث الصحيحين «اقتلوا الأسودين في الصلاة الحية والعقرب (۱) وفي صحيح مسلم مرفوعاً أمر عليه الصلاة والسلام بقتل الكلب العقور والحية والعقرب في الصلاة وأقل مراتب الأمر الإباحة. وفي شرح منية المصلي : ويستحب قتل العقرب بالنعل اليسرى إن أمكن لحديث أبي داود كذلك، ولا بأس بقياس الحية على العقرب في هذا ا.هـ. أطلقه فشمل جميع أنواع الحيات وصححه في الهداية لإطلاق الحديث وجميع المواضع وفي المحيط قالوا وينبغي أن لا تقتل الحية البيضاء التي تمشي مستوية لأنها جان لقوله عليه السلام) اقتلوا ذا الطفيتين والأبتر وإياكم والحية البيضاء فإنها من الجن (۲). وقال الطحاوي: لا بأس بقتل الكل لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عهد مع الجن أن لا يدخلوا بيوت أمته وإذا دخلوا لم يظهروا لهم فإذا دخلوا فقد نقضوا العهد فلا ذمة لهم. والأولى هو الإعذار والإنذار فيقال ارجع بإذن الله فإن أبى قتله ا هـ. يعني الإنذار في غير الصلاة. وفي النهاية معزياً إلى صدر الإسلام والصحيح من الجواب أن يحتاط في قتل الحيات حتى لا يقتل جنياً فإنهم يؤذونه أذاء كثيراً بل إذا رأى حية وشك أنه جني يقول له خل طريق المسلمين ومر، فإن مرت تركه فإن واحداً من إخواني هو أكبر سناً مني قتل حية
His statement: 'Nor the killing of the snake and scorpion' meaning it is not disliked to kill them because of the hadith in the two Sahihs: 'Kill the two black ones in prayer: the snake and the scorpion.' And in Sahih Muslim, raised: He (peace be upon him) ordered the killing of the rabid dog, the snake, and the scorpion during prayer, and the least rank of a command is permissibility. In Sharh Munyat al-Musalli: It is recommended to kill the scorpion with the left shoe if possible, due to the hadith of Abu Dawud similarly, and there is no harm in analogy of the snake to the scorpion in this. End quote. He [the author of Kanz] made it general, so it includes all types of snakes, and this was declared sound in al-Hidayah due to the generality of the hadith. In al-Muhit: They said: One should not kill the white snake that walks straight because it is a jinn, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Kill the one with two black lines and the one with a cut tail, but beware of the white snake for it is from the jinn.' Al-Tahawi said: There is no harm in killing all because the Prophet (peace be upon him) made a covenant with the jinn that they would not enter the houses of his ummah, and if they enter they do not appear to them, so if they enter they have broken the covenant and have no protection. The better way is to give an excuse and warning by saying: 'Return with Allah's permission; if he refuses, kill him.' End quote. Meaning the warning is outside prayer. In al-Nihayah, attributing to Sadr al-Islam, the correct answer is that one should be cautious in killing snakes so as not to kill a jinn, for they harm him greatly. Rather, if he sees a snake and suspects it is a jinn, he should say to it: 'Leave the way of the Muslims and go.' If it passes, he leaves it. Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq comments on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding what is not disliked in prayer. The matn says 'لا قتل الحية والعقرب' meaning it is not disliked to kill a snake or scorpion during prayer. The sharh provides evidence: a hadith from the Sahihayn (Bukhari and Muslim) orders killing the two black ones: snake and scorpion. Since the command's minimum level is ibaha (permissibility), killing them is allowed. Further, in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli, it is recommended (mustahabb) to kill a scorpion with the left shoe if possible, analogizing the snake to the scorpion. The author notes that the ruling applies to all snakes, as the hadith is general. However, a caution is given from al-Muhit: one should not kill a white snake that walks straight because it might be a jinn, citing a hadith about the white snake being from the jinn. Al-Tahawi disagreed, saying all snakes can be killed because the covenant with jinn is that they do not enter homes or show themselves, so if they appear, they have broken the covenant. The preferred position (al-ula) is to warn the snake first (outside prayer) by saying 'Return with Allah's permission'; if it persists, then kill it. In prayer, the warning is not possible, but the text implies that if in doubt, one should avoid killing. The final opinion from al-Nihayah/Sadr al-Islam is to be cautious and not kill if the snake might be a jinn, but to command it to leave. If it leaves, leave it. The anecdote of an older brother who killed a snake and was harmed illustrates the danger. Thus, the ruling: killing snakes and scorpions in prayer is permissible, even recommended for scorpions, but one must be wary of killing a jinn in snake form.

Key Terms
الحية (al-hayyah): Snake; considered a pest that can be killed in prayer.
العقرب (al-‘aqrab): Scorpion; recommended to kill in prayer if possible.
الجن (al-jinn): Invisible beings; some snakes are believed to be jinn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on killing a scorpion during prayer?
A) It is forbidden (haram) and invalidates the prayer.
B) It is permissible and even recommended (mustahabb).
C) It is disliked (makruh) but does not invalidate.
D) It is obligatory (wajib).

Key Takeaway
Killing snakes and scorpions during prayer is allowed by hadith (mubah for snakes, mustahabb for scorpions), but caution is advised for white snakes that may be jinn.

Killing a Snake During Prayer: Permissibility vs. Validity
Ruling on killing a snake during prayer and its effect on prayer validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing a snake during prayer and explain why the prayer becomes invalid with excessive movement while the killing remains permissible.

Core Idea
Killing a snake during prayer is permitted, but if it involves excessive movement, the prayer becomes invalid — the command removes sin, not invalidity.

Imagine you are in the middle of prayer and a dangerous snake appears. Your instinct is to kill it, but excessive movement could break your prayer. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq navigates the tension between following the command to kill harmful creatures and preserving the validity of prayer, settling on a nuanced view: the killing is permissible, but if it requires many actions, the prayer becomes invalid yet the killing is still not sinful.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
Determine the act: killing a snake during prayer. Establish the default permission based on the command to kill harmful animals. The passage initially states the ruling is general, covering even extensive actions.
The base text (Kanz al-Daqaiq) likely stated that killing a snake is permitted, but the commentary expands on the effect of excessive movement.
2
Explore the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Identify the two positions: Al-Sarakhsi argued that even with much action the prayer remains valid, citing analogous licenses (walking after hadath, drawing water). Later authorities (al-Nihayah, Fath al-Qadir) objected, asserting that the established narrations do not permit excessive action and that the analogy to treating a passerby (which invalidates) is more direct.
This is a classic example of conflict between qiyas (analogy) and the transmitted texts (riwaya).
3
Analyse the proof: analogical reasoning
The later authorities draw an analogy: just as treating a passerby during prayer (a commanded act) invalidates the prayer if excessive, so does killing a snake. The command removes sin but does not preserve validity. They also refer to the prayer of fear where fighting invalidates the prayer but is permissible.
The underlying principle: a command to act does not automatically override the rules of prayer invalidators; it only removes culpability.
4
Apply the principle to determine the mufta bihi
The text concludes 'thumma al-haqq fima yazharu al-fasad' (the correct view is that it invalidates). The prayer becomes fasid (invalid) if excessive movement occurs, but the killing remains permissible because the command supersedes the normal prohibition of excessive action.
Practically, the mufta bihi is: prayer invalid if amal kathir, but no sin for the killing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كبيرة بسيف في دار لنا فضربه الجن حتى جعلوه زمناً كان لا يتحرك رجلاه قريباً من الشهر ثم عالجناه وداويناه بإرضاء الجن حتى تركوه فزال ما به وهذا مما عاينته بعيني ا هـ. وأطلق في القتل فشمل ما إذا كان بعمل كثير . قال السرخسي : وهو الأظهر لأن هذا عمل رخص فيه للمصلي كالمشي بعد الحدث والاستقاء من البئر والتوضؤ ا هـ. وتعقبه في النهاية بأنه مخالف لما عليه عامة رواية شروح الجامع الصغير ورواية مبسوط شيخ الإسلام فإنهم لم يبيحوا العمل الكثير في قتلها اهـ. وتعقبه أيضاً في فتح القدير بأنه يقضي أن الاستقاء غير مفسد في سبق الحدث وقد تقدم خلافه وبحثه بأنه لا يفسد للرخصة بالنص يستلزم مثله في علاج المار إذا كثر فإنه أيضاً مأمور به بالنص كما قدمناه لكنه مفسد عندهم، فما هو جوابه عن علاج المار هو جوابنا في قتل الحية. ثم الحق فيما يظهر الفساد وقولهم الأمر بالقتال لا يستلزم بقاء الصحة على نهج ما قالوه من الفساد في صلاة الخوف إذا قاتلوا في الصلاة بل أثره في رفع الإثم بمباشرة المفسد في الصلاة بعد أن كان حراماً صحيح ا هـ.
[A story:] A large snake in our house with a sword, and the jinn struck him until they made him disabled, his legs could not move for nearly a month. Then we treated him by appeasing the jinn until they left him, and he recovered. I witnessed this with my own eyes. He said: The ruling [on killing] is general, so it includes killing with much action. Al-Sarakhsi said: That is the more apparent view, because this action is permitted for the praying person, like walking after passing water, drawing water from a well, and performing ablution. It was objected in al-Nihayah that this contradicts the general transmission of the commentaries on al-Jami' al-Saghir and the transmission of al-Mabsut of Shaykh al-Islam, for they did not permit much action in killing it. It was also objected in Fath al-Qadir that it implies that drawing water does not invalidate after the occurrence of an event, which has been previously differed upon, and he discussed that it does not invalidate because of the textual license would necessitate a similar ruling in the case of treating a passerby if it is much, for that is also commanded by the text as we mentioned, yet it invalidates according to them. So their answer regarding treating the passerby is our answer regarding killing the snake. Then the correct view is that it invalidates, and their statement that the command to fight does not necessitate preservation of validity is in accordance with what they said regarding the invalidity in the prayer of fear when they fight during prayer; rather its effect is to remove sin by directly performing an invalidator in prayer after it was forbidden. It is sound. End quote.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and discussion. It begins with a witnessed story from a scholar involving killing a large snake during prayer, noting that the action was extensive. The primary ruling is that killing a snake during prayer is permitted, but the text explores whether killing it with excessive movement invalidates the prayer. Al-Sarakhsi held that it does not invalidate because such actions are licensed for the praying person, analogous to walking to relieve oneself or drawing water. However, later sources in the Hanafi school (al-Nihayah, Fath al-Qadir) objected, stating that the established position in the early texts (zahir al-riwayah) does not permit excessive action in killing a snake, just as treating a passerby with much action invalidates prayer despite being commanded. The correct and relied-upon view (al-haqq) is that the prayer is invalidated (fasid) by much action, but the act of killing is nonetheless permissible because the command to kill the snake supersedes the normal prohibition of invalidating actions in prayer, similar to the case of fighting in the prayer of fear where the prayer is invalid but the fighting is permissible. The practical result: if one kills a snake with minimal action, the prayer remains valid; if with much action, the prayer becomes invalid but the killing is not sinful due to necessity.

Key Terms
عمل كثير (amal kathir): Excessive physical action during prayer, beyond the usual permissible movements, which invalidates the prayer according to the Hanafi school.
فساد (fasad): Invalidity of prayer due to a deficiency that cannot be compensated, requiring repetition of the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) in this passage, what is the ruling if a person kills a snake with excessive movement during prayer?
A) The prayer is valid and the killing is permissible.
B) The prayer is invalid and the killing is not permissible.
C) The prayer is invalid but the killing is permissible.
D) The prayer is valid but the killing is not permissible.

Key Takeaway
Killing a snake during prayer is permitted, but if it involves excessive movement, the prayer becomes invalid; the command removes sin, not invalidity.

Killing a Louse or Flea During Prayer: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on killing insects during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the opinions of the three Hanafi imams regarding killing a louse during prayer and apply the harmonized ruling based on presence of harm.

Core Idea
Killing a louse in prayer is disliked unless it harms you—then all three imams allow it.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the differing views of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani on whether and how to handle lice or fleas during salah. While snakes and scorpions have a clear permissibility when harmful, lice and fleas are more nuanced. The text reconciles the ikhtilaf by distinguishing between harmful and non-harmful situations and considering the location (mosque vs. outside). Understanding this dispute helps the mufti apply the ruling that best preserves focus and avoids unnecessary handling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three imams' positions
List the specific ruling of each: Abu Hanifa (dislikes killing, prefers burial), Abu Yusuf (both killing and burial disliked), Muhammad (killing preferred, either permissible).
Pay attention to the nuance: Abu Hanifa considers killing blameworthy (asa'a), but Muhammad sees no harm.
2
Determine the key factor for harmonization
The text distinguishes between when the insect causes harm (e.g., biting) and when it does not. Apply the principle: handling is permissible when harmful, disliked otherwise.
Harm nullifies the dislike because the act becomes necessary for focus.
3
Apply the location condition
Inside the mosque, killing is permissible with minimal action, but burying is prohibited to avoid soiling the mosque. Outside, burial is allowed.
The rule about not throwing remains in the mosque is a separate etiquette.
4
Derive the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
Later scholars (like al-Halabi) prefer Muhammad's view when harmful. When not harmful, avoid all handling to exit the ikhtilaf.
This is a precautionary (ihtiyat) approach: staying safe from any disliked act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي النهاية معزياً إلى الجامع الصغير البرهاني : إنما يباح قتلها في الصلاة إذا مرت بين يديه وخاف أن تؤذيه وإلا فيكره وقيد بالحية والعقرب لأن في قتل القملة والبرغوث اختلافاً قال في الظهيرية : فإن أخذ قملة في الصلاة كره له أن يقتلها لكن يدفنها تحت الحصى وهو قول أبي حنيفة، وروي عنه إذا أخذ قملة أو برغوثاً فقتله أو دفنه فقد أساء، وعن محمد إنه يقتلها وقتلها أحب إلى من دفنها وأي ذلك فعل فلا بأس به. وقال أبو يوسف: يكره كلاهما في الصلاة ا هـ. وذكر في شرح منية المصلي أن دفنهما مكروه في المسجد في غير الصلاة. وأن الحاصل أنه يكره التعرض لكل منهما بالأخذ فضلاً عن القتل أو الدفن عند عدم تعرضهما له بالأذى، وأما عند تعرضهما له بالأذى فإن كان خارج المسجد فلا بأس حينئذ بالأخذ والقتل أو الدفن بعد أن لا يكون ذلك بعمل كثير فإن كان خارج المسجد فلا بأس حينئذ بالأخذ والقتل أو الدفن بعد أن لا يكون ذلك بعمل كثير فإنه كما روي عن ابن مسعود من دفنها روي عن أنس أنهم كانوا يقتلون القمل والبراغيث في الصلاة، ولعل أبا حنيفة إنما اختار الدفن على القتل لما فيه من النزاهة عن إصابة دمهما ليد القاتل أو ثوبه في هذه الحالة وإن كان ذلك معفواً عنه ، وأن ابن مسعود فعل أحسن الجائزين وإن كان في المسجد فلا بأس بالقتل بالشرط المذكور ولا يطرحها في المسجد بطريق الدفن ولا غيره إلا إذا غلب على ظنه أنه يظفر يقال بكراهتها، وفي اقتصار المؤلف وصاحب الحاوي القدسي عليها إشعار بذلك . بها بعد الفراغ من الصلاة وبهذا التفصيل يحصل الجمع بين ما عنه أنه لو دفنها في المسجد فقد أساء ا هـ. في الصلاة وبين ما عن أبي حنيفة من أنه يدفنها
And in al-Nihayah, attributed to al-Jami' al-Saghir al-Burhani: It is only permissible to kill it during prayer if it passes between his hands and he fears it will harm him; otherwise it is disliked. It was restricted to the snake and scorpion because there is disagreement regarding killing the louse and flea. He said in al-Zahiriyyah: If one takes a louse in prayer, it is disliked for him to kill it, but he should bury it under gravel, and that is the saying of Abu Hanifah. It is narrated from him that if he took a louse or flea and killed it or buried it, he has done wrong. From Muhammad: He kills it, and killing it is more beloved to me than burying it; whichever he does, there is no harm. Abu Yusuf said: Both are disliked in prayer. End quote. It is mentioned in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli that burying them is disliked in the mosque outside of prayer. And the conclusion is that it is disliked to handle either of them by taking, let alone killing or burying, when they do not cause harm. As for when they cause harm, if outside the mosque, then there is no harm in taking, killing, or burying, provided that is not with much action. If outside the mosque, there is no harm in taking, killing, or burying, provided that is not with much action, as it is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud that he buried it, and from Anas that they used to kill lice and fleas in prayer. Perhaps Abu Hanifah chose burying over killing because of the propriety of avoiding the blood reaching the killer's hand or garment in that state, even though it is pardoned. And Ibn Mas'ud did the better of two permissible acts. If inside the mosque, then there is no harm in killing with the mentioned condition, and he should not throw it in the mosque by burying or otherwise, unless he thinks it is likely to be caught. It is said that it is disliked, and the restriction of the author and the author of al-Hawi al-Qudsi to that indicates such. After finishing the prayer, this detail reconciles the transmission that if he buried it in the mosque he has done wrong, and the transmission from Abu Hanifah that he buries it.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding killing a louse or flea during prayer. The base ruling per al-Nihayah is that killing a snake or scorpion is permissible only if it crosses in front and one fears harm; otherwise it is disliked. However, the passage distinguishes fee from other insects because of disagreement. The opinions of the three Hanafi imams: Abu Hanifa says it is disliked to kill a louse; instead one should bury it under gravel. According to one transmission, if one kills or buries it, one does wrong (asa'a). Muhammad al-Shaybani prefers killing to burying, and says either is permissible without harm. Abu Yusuf holds that both killing and burying are disliked. The consensus of later commentators is that when the insect does not cause harm, handling it at all (taking, killing, burying) is disliked, whether inside or outside the mosque. If it causes harm (e.g., biting), then it is permissible to take, kill, or bury, provided it does not involve excessive movement. Outside the mosque, no restriction beyond that. Inside the mosque, killing is permissible under the same condition, but one should not throw it or bury it there; rather he should remove it carefully. The reconciliation between contradictory narrations from Abu Hanifa is that his ruling was for a non-harmful situation; if harm is present, killing or burying is permissible. The text also notes that Abu Hanifa's preference for burying was to avoid blood on hands or clothes, though that is usually excusable. The practical takeaway: if one is bitten or pestered, killing is permissible; otherwise, it is better to avoid all handling.

Key Terms
قملة (qumla): A louse, a small parasitic insect that may be found on the body or clothes.
برغوث (barghuth): A flea, another bothersome insect, similar ruling to lice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which Hanafi imam considers killing a louse during prayer as preferable to burying it?
A) Abu Hanifa
B) Abu Yusuf
C) Muhammad al-Shaybani
D) Al-Sarakhsi

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's ruling on killing insects during prayer depends on whether the insect is harming you; if not, it is best to leave it alone and avoid handling.

Ruling on Praying Towards the Back or Face of a Person
Ruling with proof on praying towards back vs face

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for praying towards the back of a sitting person and distinguish it from praying towards the face, applying the Hanafi principle of tarjih.

Core Idea
Praying towards someone's back is permissible; praying towards their face is disliked – direction matters.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the Hanafi ruling on a common concern: what is the ruling if one prays towards a person who is sitting or lying? The text distinguishes between praying towards the back (zahr) and the face (wajh), providing evidence from the hadith of Aisha (radiyallahu anha) and addressing an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. By understanding this ruling, you will be able to apply the correct fiqh in your daily prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the act: praying towards the back of a sitting person who is talking. The initial ruling from al-Jami' al-Saghir is that it is not disliked (la tukrah).
2
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Recognize the contrary narration from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad reporting from Abu Hanifa that it is disliked, based on a hadith from Ibn Abbas.
This is a weaker opinion within the school.
3
Examine the dalil
Analyze the strong evidence: the hadith of Aisha in Sahihayn where she lay between the Prophet and the qiblah during his night prayer, and he did not prohibit her. This indicates permissibility.
The hadith is qati' al-thubut and zanni al-dalala.
4
Understand the tarjih
The commentator gives precedence to the hadith of Aisha over the weaker hadith from al-Bazzar. The disliked case is limited to when disturbance is feared.
This is the mufta bihi position.
5
Distinguish the ruling for the face
The passage explicitly states that praying towards someone's face is disliked (makruh tanzih). This applies both ways: the worshipper facing a person's face and the person facing the worshipper's face.
The dislike is from both sides.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

النيام والمحدثين وأجيب بأنه محمول في النائمين على ما إذا خاف ظهور صوت منهم يضحكه ويخجل النائم إذا انتبه، وفي المحدثين على ما إذا كان لهم أصوات يخاف منها التغليط أو شغل البال، ونحن نقول بالكراهة في هذا ثم يعارض الحديث المذكور في النائمين ويقدم عليه لقوته ما في الصحيحين عن عائشة قالت: كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي صلاة الليل كلها وأنا معترضة بينه وبين القبلة، فإذا أراد أن يوتر أيقظني فأوترت. وإنما قيد بقوله «يتحدث» ليفيد عدم الكراهة إلى ظهر من لا يتحدث بالأولى ولعله متفق عليه وقد كان يفعله ابن عمر إذا لم يجد سارية يقول لنافع : ول ظهرك. وأفاد كلامهم هنا أنه لا كراهة على المتحدث ولهذا نقل كما في الجامع الصغير. قال في المنية والاستقبال إلى المصلي مكروه، سواء كان المصلي في الصف الأول أو في الصف الأخير ولهذا قال في الذخيرة : يكره للإمام أن يستقبل المصلي وإن كان بينهما صفوف وهذا هو ظاهر المذهب ذكره في الفصل الرابع من كتاب الصلاة والحاصل أن استقبال المصلي إلى وجه الإنسان مكروه واستقبال الإنسان وجه المصلي مكروه فالكراهة من الجانبين. قال العلامة الحلبي : وقد صرحوا بأنه لو صلى إلى وجه ويحمل ما عن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف على الأخذ من غير عذر أي القرص قوله : ولعله متفق عليه) أي عدم الكراهة إلى ظهر من لا يتحدث وفي شرح المنية للشيخ إبراهيم وقوله يتحدث لإفادة نفي قول من قال بالكراهة بحضرة المتحدثين، وكذا بحضرة النائمين وما روي عنه عليه الصلاة والسلام لا تصلوا خلف النائم ولا متحدث (۱) ضعيف وتمامه فيه قوله : (وقد صرحوا الخ) أي لأن الثالث صار كالفاصل كما في النهر قال وقياسه أنه لو صلى إلى His saying: (And praying towards the back of a sitting person who is talking means it is not disliked, as in al-Jami' al-Saghir. And in the narration of al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa: It is disliked for him to pray while before him there are sleeping people or people talking, because of what al-Bazzar narrated from Ibn Abbas marfu'an: 'I was forbidden to pray facing sleeping people and people engaged in conversation.' And it is answered that it is interpreted regarding sleepers as when he fears an appearance of a voice from them that would make him laugh and embarrass the sleeper when he wakes up, and regarding people talking as when they have voices that one fears cause mistakes or occupy the mind. And we say that there is dislike in that case. Then the hadith mentioned regarding sleepers is contradicted and outweighed in strength by what is in the two Sahihs from Aisha who said: The Messenger of Allah used to pray the night prayer entirely while I was lying between him and the qiblah; when he wanted to perform witr, he would wake me up and I would pray witr. He restricted the ruling by his saying 'who is talking' to indicate that there is no dislike in praying towards the back of someone who is not talking, and it is rather agreed upon. And Ibn Umar used to do that when he could not find a pillar: he would say to Nafi': Face your back to me. Their statement here indicates that there is no dislike on the part of the person talking, and therefore the commentator related from the Companions that some of them were reciting the Quran, some were discussing knowledge and exhortations, and some were praying, and the Prophet did not forbid them; if it had been disliked, he would have forbidden them. End quote. He restricted by 'back' because praying towards the face of someone is disliked, as in al-Jami' al-Saghir. He said in al-Munyah: Facing the worshipper is disliked, whether the worshipper is in the first row or the last row; therefore it is said in al-Dhakhirah: It is disliked for the imam to face the worshipper even if there are rows between them, and that is the apparent position of the madhhab, mentioned in the fourth chapter of the Book of Prayer. The outcome is that the worshipper facing the face of a person is disliked, and the person facing the face of the worshipper is disliked; so dislike is from both sides. Al-Halabi said: They have explicitly stated that if one prays facing the face of a person... (the rest is commentary on the previous section about lice and the ruling on praying towards a high place).
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding two related issues: praying towards the back of a sitting person who is talking, and praying towards someone's face. It begins by stating, from al-Jami' al-Saghir, that praying towards the back of a sitting person who is talking is not disliked. A contrary narration from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad from Abu Hanifa says it is disliked based on a hadith prohibiting prayer in front of sleeping or talking people. The commentator reconciles: the hadith applies only if the sleeper or speaker might disturb the prayer (e.g., laughing or loud conversation). When no such disturbance exists, the majority position is that it is not disliked. Strong evidence for this comes from the authentic hadith of Aisha, in which she lay between the Prophet and the qiblah during his night prayer, and he did not prohibit her. Similarly, the practice of Ibn Umar and the Companions shows that it is permitted. The passage then clearly states that praying towards someone's face is disliked, according to al-Jami' al-Saghir and other sources. The dislike applies both to the worshipper facing a person's face and to the person facing the worshipper's face. Exceptions are mentioned: if the person is on a high place and only visible when standing, not when sitting, then it is not disliked, as that person acts as a divider (faasil) rather than an object of facing. The commentary also ties back to the louse discussion, noting that if one is bitten, the best action is to kill (following Muhammad's view) to preserve focus.

Key Terms
ظهر (zahr): The back of a person; praying towards the back of a seated person is not disliked.
مكروه (makruh): Disliked (tanzihi) – an action whose avoidance is rewarded but not sinful to perform.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in this passage, what is the ruling for praying towards the back of a person who is sitting and talking?
A) It is disliked (makruh tanzih).
B) It is not disliked (mubah).
C) It is obligatory (wajib).
D) It invalidates the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The direction of the person matters: pray towards their back is permissible, pray towards their face is disliked.

Praying Towards a Mushaf or Sword: Permissibility
Commentary explaining that praying towards a Mushaf or sword is not disliked

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying towards a Mushaf or sword and explain the proofs used.

Core Idea
Neither a Mushaf nor a sword before the worshipper makes the prayer disliked; both are permissible based on veneration and prophetic practice.

It is common to wonder whether placing a copy of the Qur'an or a weapon in front of oneself during prayer affects its validity or acceptability. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position: it is not disliked. We will examine the reasoning and the scriptural evidence that supports this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is praying while a Mushaf or a sword is placed in front (hanging or on the ground). The ruling is that it is not disliked (laysa bi-makruh).
2
Locate the dalil for the sword
The Prophet ﷺ prayed facing a spear (al-'anaza), which is a weapon. Swords are similar to spears in being weapons, so the same permissibility applies.
Dalil is a hadith (Sunnah ahad).
3
Understand the dalil for the Mushaf
No direct hadith is cited; instead, the reasoning is that honouring the Mushaf by placing it before the worshipper is an act of worship, which joins another worship (prayer) without causing disliked resemblance.
The objection of tashabbuh (resembling People of the Book) is rejected because their intention is reading, not veneration.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action of praying towards a spear indicates that facing a weapon is permissible. Since the Mushaf is an object of veneration, it is even more commendable.
The illa (effective cause) for the sword is 'being a weapon', which applies to swords.
5
Note the objection and Hanafi response
Objection: it resembles the People of the Book who place scripture before them. Response: they do so to read, whereas Muslims do so to venerate; the intention changes the ruling.
This is an example of rejecting an invalid analogy (qiyas fasid).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وإلى مصحف أو سيف معلق) أي لا يكره أن يصلي وأمامه مصحف أو سيف، سواء كان معلقاً أو بين يديه. أما المصحف فلأن في تقديمه تعظيمه وتعظيمه عبادة والاستخفاف به كفر فانضمت هذه العبادة إلى عبادة أخرى فلا قال بالكراهة إذا كان معلقاً معللاً بأنه تشبه بأهل الكتاب مردود لأن أهل الكتاب يفعلونه للقراءة منه وليس كلا منا فيه. وأما السيف فلأنه سلاح ولا يكره التوجه إليه فقد النبي ﷺ كان يصلي إلى العنزة وهي سلاح.
His statement: (And towards a Mushaf or a hanging sword) meaning it is not disliked that one prays while a Mushaf or sword is in front of him, whether it is hanging or before him. As for the Mushaf, because presenting it is honoring it, and honoring it is worship, and disrespecting it is disbelief. So this worship is joined to another worship, hence no one said it is disliked if it is hanging, claiming it resembles the People of the Book. This is rejected because the People of the Book do it for reading from it, and not all of us are in that. As for the sword, because it is a weapon, and it is not disliked to face it, for the Prophet ﷺ used to pray facing a spear (al-'anaza), which is a weapon.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The commentator explains that the matn's ruling—praying towards a Mushaf (copy of the Qur'an) or a hanging sword—is not disliked. For the Mushaf, the reasoning is that placing it in front is an act of veneration, which is worship; joining worship to worship is commendable, not disliked. The objection that it resembles the practice of the People of the Book (who place scripture before them in prayer) is rejected because they do so for reading, while the Muslim does so for reverence. For the sword, the proof is that the Prophet ﷺ prayed facing a spear (al-'anaza), as recorded in authentic hadith. Thus, both are permissible.

Key Terms
مصحف (mushaf): A physical copy of the Qur'an
سيف (sayf): A sword, considered a weapon (silah)
كراهة (karaha): Dislike; here it means the ruling of being makruh (disliked), which is negated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on praying towards a Mushaf (copy of the Qur'an) that is hanging or placed in front?
A) It is makruh tanzihi
B) It is makruh tahrimi
C) It is not disliked
D) It is haram

Key Takeaway
Praying towards a Mushaf or sword is not disliked; the Mushaf is venerated, and the sword is proven by the Prophet's practice.
