Performing and Making Up Witr: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Details rulings on performing witr while sitting/riding and its qada, with differences among Hanafi imams

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement on the status of witr (wajib vs sunnah mu'akkadah) and identify the practical differences in its performance and qada.

Core Idea
Witr is wajib according to Abu Hanifa and sunnah mu'akkadah according to his two companions, yet they agree on prohibition of performing it on a riding animal and on the obligation of making it up.

This lesson explores the ruling on performing witr while sitting or riding, and the obligation to make it up if missed. The three Hanafi imams differ on whether witr is wajib (Abu Hanifa) or sunnah mu'akkadah (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). Despite this difference, they agree on some key rulings but diverge on the timing of qada. By examining the proofs and practical consequences, you will understand how this dispute shapes Hanafi practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the three positions
Determine the central question: What is the legal status of witr? State the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.
2
Analyse the evidence for each position
Examine the hadith cited in the passage and the Prophet's practice. Understand how each imam uses the same evidence to support their view.
Both sides use the hadith 'من نام عن وتر أو نسيه فليصله إذا ذكره' but interpret it differently.
3
Identify points of agreement
Note that despite the status dispute, all three agree that witr cannot be performed sitting (if able to stand) or on a riding animal without excuse, and that qada is obligatory.
4
Pinpoint the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
The key difference is the time when qada can be performed. Abu Hanifa allows qada after Fajr before sunrise and after Asr; the two companions do not.
This stems from the classification: qada of wajib is allowed at makruh times, but qada of sunnah is not.
5
Evaluate the tarjih and mufta bihi
Understand why the Hanafi school adopts Abu Hanifa's view as the relied-upon position, and how the objection in Fath al-Qadir is refuted.
The tarjih authority is al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah and later scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي المحيط : لا يجوز الوتر قاعداً مع القدرة على القيام ولا على راحلته من غير عذر لأن عنده الوتر واجب وأداء الواجبات والفرائض على الراحلة من غير عذر لا يجوز، وعندهما وإن كان سنة لكن صح عن النبي الله أنه كان يتنفل على راحلته من غير عذر في الليل وإذا بلغ الوتر نزل فيوتر على الأرض .اهـ. فأفاد أنه لا يجوز قاعداً وراكباً من غير عذر باتفاق أبي حنيفة وصاحبيه. وصرح في الهداية بأنه يجب قضاؤه إذا فاته بالإجماع وصححه في التجنيس، وعلل له في المحيط بقوله : أما عنده فلأنه واجب وأما عندهما فلقوله عليه السلام من نام عن وتر أو نسيه فليصله إذا ذكره » (۱) اهـ . وصرح في الكافي بأن وجوب قضائه ظاهر الرواية عنهما، وروي عنهما عدمه وسيأتي أنه لا يصلي خلف النفل اتفاقاً، فظهر بهذا أنه لا فرق بين قوله بوجوبه وبين قولهما بسنيته من جهة الأحكام فإن السنة المؤكدة بمنزلة الواجب إلا في فساد الصبح بتذكره وفي قضائه بعد طلوع الفجر قبل طلوع الشمس . قال في التجنيس : عند أبي حنيفة يقضيه بعد طلوع الفجر قبل طلوع الشمس وبعد صلاة العصر لأنه واجب عنده فيجوز قضاؤه فيه كقضاء سائر الفرائض وعندهما لا لأنه سنة عندهما ا هـ . لكن تعقب صاحب الهداية في فتح القدير بأنه سنة عندهما فوجوب القضاء محل النزاع، وقد علمت دفعه بما في المحيط.
And in al-Muhit: It is not permissible to pray witr while sitting when able to stand, nor on one's riding animal without an excuse, because according to him (Abu Hanifa) witr is wajib, and performing wajibat and fara'id on a riding animal without excuse is not permissible. And according to them (the two companions), even if it is sunnah, it is authentically reported from the Prophet that he would offer supererogatory prayers on his riding animal without excuse at night, and when he reached witr, he would dismount and pray witr on the ground. End. So it indicates that it is not permissible while sitting or riding without excuse by agreement of Abu Hanifa and his two companions. And it is explicitly stated in al-Hidayah that its qada is obligatory if missed, by consensus, and al-Tajniss authenticated it, and he justified it in al-Muhit by saying: As for him (Abu Hanifa), because it is wajib; and as for them (the two companions), because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever sleeps through witr or forgets it, let him pray it when he remembers it.' End. And it is explicitly stated in al-Kafi that the obligation of its qada is the apparent narration from them, and it is also narrated from them that it is not (obligatory). And it will come that one cannot pray behind a supererogatory prayer by agreement. So it appears from this that there is no difference between his saying it is wajib and their saying it is sunnah in terms of rulings, for the sunnah mu'akkadah is like wajib, except in the invalidation of fajr by remembering it and in its qada after dawn before sunrise. He said in al-Tajniss: According to Abu Hanifa, he prays it after dawn before sunrise and after Asr prayer, because it is wajib according to him, so its qada is permissible in these times, like qada of other obligations. And according to them, no, because it is sunnah according to them. End. But the author of al-Hidayah in Fath al-Qadir objected that according to them it is sunnah, so the obligation of qada is a point of dispute. And you have known the refutation of that by what is in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the rulings of performing and making up witr. It begins with a ruling from al-Muhit: Witr cannot be performed sitting if one can stand, nor on a riding animal without excuse. This is agreed upon by all three Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) despite their difference on the status of witr (wajib vs sunnah). The reason for the agreement: Abu Hanifa considers it wajib, so performing it on a riding animal is invalid; the two companions consider it sunnah, but the Prophet himself dismounted for witr, indicating a special status. Next, the passage discusses qada (makeup) of witr. Al-Hidayah states that qada is obligatory by consensus, citing the hadith: 'Whoever sleeps through witr or forgets it, let him pray it when he remembers it.' This hadith is used by both sides: Abu Hanifa uses it as proof of obligation; the two companions use it to show that qada is recommended. In al-Kafi, the obligation of qada is the apparent narration from the two companions, but another narration says no. The passage then synthesizes: despite the difference on the original obligation, in practice there is little difference in rulings except in two cases: (1) remembering an outstanding witr during fajr prayer (it invalidates fajr only according to Abu Hanifa? Actually, the text says 'فساد الصبح بتذكره' meaning the invalidation of the fajr prayer by remembering it), and (2) the time for qada: according to Abu Hanifa, witr can be made up after dawn before sunrise and after Asr, because it is like other obligations; according to the two companions, it cannot, because it is sunnah. However, the author of al-Hidayah in Fath al-Qadir raises an objection: if it is sunnah according to them, then the obligation of qada is itself disputed. The passage notes that this objection is refuted by the earlier citation from al-Muhit (which includes the hadith).

Key Terms
القضاء (al-qada): Performing a missed obligatory prayer after its prescribed time.
السنة المؤكدة (al-sunnah al-mu'akkadah): A confirmed sunnah that the Prophet consistently performed and rarely left, considered like wajib in many rulings except in invalidation and qada timing.
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after Isha, consisting typically of 3 rak'ats.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when can witr be made up if missed?
A) Only before Fajr.
B) After Fajr before sunrise and after Asr.
C) At any time except sunrise, zenith, and sunset.
D) Only at night.

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi disagreement on the status of witr (wajib vs sunnah mu'akkadah) does not affect the obligation to make it up, but it does affect the time when it can be made up.

Enforcement of Collective Abandonment of Witr and Sunan
Ruling on enforcement of collective abandonment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on collective abandonment of witr and sunan, and distinguish the conditions that lead to disciplinary action versus apostasy.

Core Idea
Abandoning witr leads to discipline and imprisonment; abandoning sunan with contempt leads to fighting.

In this lesson, we explore a unique Hanafi ruling: what happens when an entire community collectively abandons certain prayers? The passage distinguishes between witr (wajib) and sunan (recommended but established), and shows that the imam's response escalates from discipline to imprisonment to fighting—but only when the abandonment reflects contempt, not mere neglect. Understanding this ruling clarifies the delicate balance between enforcing religious practices and avoiding excessive force.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their legal categories
Witr is wajib, sunan (like adhan, siwak) are sunnah mu'akkadah or ghayr mu'akkadah. Note the difference in enforcement.
2
Analyze the escalation of enforcement for witr
First discipline (ta'dib), then imprisonment (habs), then fighting (qital) if they persist. This is for collective abandonment.
3
Analyze the enforcement for sunan
The imam fights them as he would for fara'id, based on the transmission from Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak.
This applies only if they abandon with contempt (jafaa) while acknowledging its truth.
4
Understand the nuance of jafaa
Jafaa means contemptuous neglect while still holding the practice as true. If they deny its truth (inkar), they become apostates.
Al-Khulasa clarifies this distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الظهيرية والولوالجية والتجنيس وغيرهما أهل قرية اجتمعوا على ترك الوتر أدبهم الإمام وحبسهم فإن لم يمتنعوا قاتلهم، وإن امتنعوا عن أداء السنن فجواب أئمة بخارى بأن الإمام يقاتلهم كما يقاتلهم على ترك الفرائض لما روي عن عبد الله المبارك أنه بن قال : لو أن أهل بلدة أنكروا سنة السواك لقاتلتهم كما نقاتل المرتدين اهـ. وفي العمدة: اجتمع قوم على ترك الأذان يؤدبهم الإمام وعلى ترك السنن يقاتلهم . زاد في الخلاصة بأن هذا إذا تركها جفاء لكن رآها حقاً فإن لم يرها حقاً يكفر .
And in al-Zahiriyya, al-Walwalijiyya, al-Tajniss, and others: The people of a village collectively abandoning witr—the imam disciplines them and imprisons them; if they do not desist, he fights them. And if they abstain from performing the sunan, the response of the imams of Bukhara is that the imam fights them as he fights them for abandoning obligations, because of what was narrated from Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak that he said: 'If the people of a town denied the sunnah of the siwak, I would fight them as we fight apostates.' End. And in al-Umda: A group collectively abandoning the adhan—the imam disciplines them; and abandoning the sunan—he fights them. Al-Khulasa added: This is when they abandon them out of contempt but consider them true; if they do not consider them true, they become disbelievers.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the collective abandonment of witr and sunan by a community. The sources (al-Zahiriyya, al-Walwalijiyya, al-Tajniss) state that if an entire village agrees to abandon witr, the imam (ruler) should first discipline and imprison them, and if they still refuse, he fights them. This shows that witr, being wajib, is treated similarly to fard in enforcement. As for sunan (like siwak, adhan), the imams of Bukhara, citing Abdullah ibn al-Mubarak, say the imam fights them as he would for fara'id, because rejecting a known sunnah with contempt is akin to apostasy. However, al-Khulasa clarifies that this fighting is only if they abandon it out of contempt (jafaa) while still believing it to be true (haqq). If they deny its truth (i.e., reject its legitimacy), they become kafir (apostates). This nuance is crucial: the punishment depends on the intention and belief of the abandoners.

Key Terms
الجفاء (al-jafaa): Negligence or contemptuous abandonment of a religious practice while still acknowledging its validity.
السنن (al-sunan): Recommended or confirmed practices (sunan mu'akkadah and ghayr mu'akkadah) that the Prophet consistently performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Khulasa, when does abandoning sunan lead to fighting?
A) When it is done out of forgetfulness.
B) When it is done out of contempt (jafaa) while still acknowledging its truth.
C) When it is done by a single individual.
D) When it is done after sunset.

Key Takeaway
The enforcement for collective abandonment of witr is gradual (discipline, prison, fight), while for sunan it depends on jafaa: if contemptuous but not denial, fight; if denial, apostasy.

Two Types of Wajib in Hanafi Fiqh
Defines two categories of wajib: one equivalent to fard in practice, the other below fard.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two categories of wajib in Hanafi fiqh and state their different practical consequences.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, some wajibat are as strong as fard, while others are weaker and only require compensation.

The Hanafi school is unique in categorizing wajib into two subcategories. This classification, found in later works like al-Tahqiq, has real practical implications: some wajibat (like witr) can invalidate other prayers if missed, while others (like reciting al-Fatiha) only require sujud al-sahw. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying Hanafi rulings in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of wajib
Read the passage and note that the author states there are two types: one 'in the strength of fard' and one 'below fard, above sunnah'.
2
Analyse the first type: wajib with strength of fard
Focus on the example of witr according to Abu Hanifa. Understand that if someone remembers a missed witr while performing fajr, the fajr prayer becomes invalid, just as if they remembered a missed fard (Isha).
This shows that this type of wajib has the same effect as fard on other prayers.
3
Analyse the second type: wajib below fard
The example is specifying recitation of al-Fatiha. If omitted, the prayer is not invalidated, but sujud al-sahw becomes obligatory.
This type is above sunnah in rank but below fard in consequences.
4
Contrast the consequences
Compare the outcomes: omission of the first type (if remembered) invalidates the current prayer; omission of the second type requires compensation but does not invalidate.
5
Recognize the source and authority
Note that this classification is from al-Tahqiq by the author of al-Kashshaf, indicating it is a later systematization within the Hanafi school.
It is not from the earliest sources but is accepted as mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر في التحقيق لصاحب الكشف أن الواجب نوعان واجب في قوة الفرض في العمل كالوتر عند أبي حنيفة حتى منع تذكره صحة الفجر كتذكر العشاء، وواجب دون الفرض في العمل فوق السنة كتعيين الفاتحة حتى وجب سجود السهو بتركه ولكن لا تفسد الصلاة اهـ.
And it is mentioned in al-Tahqiq by the author of al-Kashshaf that al-wajib is of two types: wajib in the strength of fard in practice, like witr according to Abu Hanifa, such that remembering it prevents the validity of fajr like remembering Isha; and wajib below fard in practice, above sunnah, like the specification of al-Fatiha, such that sujud al-sahw becomes obligatory for leaving it, but it does not invalidate the prayer. End.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification (definition_ruling) of wajib from the work al-Tahqiq by the author of al-Kashshaf (likely Abu al-Barakat al-Nasafi or similar). It states that in the Hanafi school, wajib has two subcategories. The first is 'wajib in the strength of fard' (في قوة الفرض في العمل), meaning that its omission has the same effect as omitting a fard: if one remembers a missed witr while praying fajr, it invalidates fajr, just as remembering a missed Isha prayer would. This is because witr, being wajib, is treated like fard for the purpose of invalidation. The second type is 'wajib below fard' (دون الفرض في العمل), but above sunnah. An example is the recitation of Surah al-Fatiha in prayer. While it is obligatory (wajib), leaving it does not invalidate the prayer completely; rather, one must perform sujud al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) to compensate. This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school and shows the granularity of their legal system. The same act (witr) can affect other prayers, while a different wajib (Fatiha) has a milder consequence.

Key Terms
قوة الفرض (quwwat al-fard): A wajib that, in terms of its practical effect on other prayers, is equivalent to a fard. Example: witr invalidates fajr if remembered during it.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness required to compensate for omitting a wajib or for mistakes in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if one omits reciting Surah al-Fatiha in prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) Sujud al-sahw is required, but the prayer is valid.
C) The prayer is valid without any compensation.
D) The prayer is invalid if omitted intentionally.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recognizes two categories of wajib: one with the strength of fard (e.g., witr) that can invalidate other prayers, and one below fard (e.g., reciting al-Fatiha) that only requires sujud al-sahw.

Universality of the Obligation of Witr
Affirms that witr is obligatory on all legally capable Muslims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the universality of witr's obligation and identify the condition of ahl al-wujub.

Core Idea
Witr is wajib on every sane, mature Muslim — free or slave, male or female.

This lesson establishes a key principle in Hanafi fiqh: the obligation of witr prayer is not limited to a specific group. It applies to all who are legally responsible (mukallaf). Understanding this universality prevents misconceptions about who must perform witr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the passage is about witr prayer, which in the Hanafi school is wajib (obligatory but less than fard).
Witr is considered wajib, not fard, due to its zanni proof.
2
Note the scope of obligation
The passage explicitly states that it is not specific to some but encompasses all people, including free and slave, male and female.
This refutes any notion of exclusion based on social status or gender.
3
Identify the condition for obligation
The only condition is that the person is 'ahl al-wujub' – a legally capable Muslim: sane, mature, and Muslim.
This excludes non-Muslims, minors, and the insane.
4
Recognize the basis
The generality is due to the evidences (dalil) for witr being general and not specifying any subgroup.
The phrase 'لعموم الدلائل' indicates that the proofs themselves are universal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي البدائع أن وجوبه لا يختص بالبعض دون البعض بل يعم الناس أجمع من الحر والعبد والذكر والأنثى إن كان أهلاً للوجوب لعموم الدلائل .
And in al-Bada'i' that its obligation is not specific to some to the exclusion of others, but rather encompasses all people, free and slave, male and female, if they are eligible for obligation, due to the generality of the evidences.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a straightforward ruling statement from al-Bada'i' (likely al-Bada'i' al-Sana'i' by al-Kasani). It emphasizes that the obligation of witr is universal within the Muslim community. It applies to all legally responsible individuals (mukallaf): free persons and slaves, men and women. The only condition is that the person must be 'ahl al-wujub'—i.e., a sane, mature Muslim. The generality of the evidences (لموم الدلائل) means that the proofs for witr's obligation do not differentiate between these categories. This is consistent with the Hanafi view that witr is a wajib act, like other wajibat (e.g., sadaqat al-fitr), and not limited to certain groups.

Key Terms
أهل الوجوب (ahl al-wujub): The condition of being legally obligated: being a sane, mature, capable Muslim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Slaves
B) Women
C) Those not eligible for obligation (e.g., insane, child, non-Muslim)
D) Travelers

Key Takeaway
Witr is wajib on all legally capable Muslims, free or slave, male or female.

Witr: Three Rak'ahs with One Taslim and Specified Qira'ah
Ruling with proof on the form and recitation of witr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of rak'ahs and recitation in witr and defend it with the primary evidence from hadith and the school's refutation of opposing views.

Core Idea
Witr is three rak'ahs with one taslim and specific surahs – any deviation is against the established practice.

This lesson establishes the definitive Hanafi position on the form of witr prayer: exactly three rak'ahs, concluded by a single taslim, with prescribed surahs. The proof comes from a clear hadith of Aisha and the practice of the Companions. We will also address the main counter-argument and see why the Hanafi school rejects adding the mu'awwidhatayn in the third rak'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central ruling
State the Hanafi position: witr is three rak'ahs with one taslim at the end, not two separate taslims.
This contrasts with some other schools that allow one or three with two taslims.
2
Extract the primary evidence
Analyze the hadith from Aisha (ra) as quoted: the Prophet (ﷺ) prayed witr with three rak'ahs and did not make taslim except at the end.
The wording 'لا يسلم إلا في آخرهن' indicates that the three rak'ahs are continuous.
3
Analyze the counter-argument
Examine the hadith 'Night prayer is two by two, and when one fears dawn, pray one to make it witr.' Understand why it is not decisive: it can mean praying one rak'ah attached to the previous two, not an independent unit.
The Hanafi response relies on the ambiguity of this hadith against the explicit practice of the Prophet (ﷺ).
4
Identify the prescribed recitation
List the surahs: first rak'ah – Surah al-A'la (سبح اسم ربك الأعلى), second – Surah al-Kafirun (قل يا أيها الكافرون), third – Surah al-Ikhlas (قل هو الله أحد).
This is based on a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa's chain.
5
Understand the rejection of additional surahs
Note that adding the mu'awwidhatayn (Surah al-Falaq and al-Nas) is rejected by leading hadith scholars and most scholars of Islam.
The relied-upon view is to recite only Surah al-Ikhlas in the third rak'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وهو ثلاث ركعات بتسليمة) أي الوتر لما رواه الحاكم وصححه وقال على عائشة شرطهما عن رضي الله عنها قالت: كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يوتر بثلاث لا يسلم إلا في آخرهن. قيل للحسن : إن ابن عمر كان يسلم في الركعتين من الوتر فقال: كان عمر منه وكان ينهض في الثانية بالتكبير .اهـ. ونقله الطحاوي عن أصحاب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. وأما قوله صلاة الليل مثنى مثنى وإذا خشي الصبح صلى واحدة فأوترت له ما صلى فليس فيه دلالة على أن الوتر واحدة بتحريمة مستأنفة ليحتاج إلى الاشتغال بجوابه إذا يحتمل كلاً من ذلك ومن كونه إذا خشي الصبح صلى واحدة متصلة ومع الاحتمال لا يقاوم الصرائح الواردة، وقد روى الإمام أبو حنيفة بسنده أنه عليه السلام كان يقرأ في الأولى «بسبح اسم ربك الأعلى، وفي الثانية قل يا أيها الكافرون، وفي الثالثة قل هو الله أحد». وما وقع في السنن وغيرها من زيادة المعوذتين أنكرها الإمام أحمد وابن معين ولم يختارها أكثر أهل العلم كما ذكره الترمذي. كذا في شرح منية المصلي.
His saying (and it is three rak'ahs with one taslim) i.e., witr, due to what was narrated by al-Hakim and he authenticated it and said: on the authority of Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, she said: 'The Messenger of Allah used to pray witr with three rak'ahs, not making taslim except at the end of them.' It was said to al-Hasan: 'Ibn Umar used to make taslim in the two rak'ahs of witr.' He said: 'Umar was like that, and he would rise in the second with takbir.' End. And al-Tahawi transmitted it from the Companions of the Messenger of Allah. As for his saying 'Night prayer is two by two, and when he fears the dawn, he prays one, so that it becomes witr for what he has prayed,' there is no evidence in this that witr is one with an independent intention requiring engagement in answering it, because it is possible either way, including the possibility that when he fears the dawn, he prays one connectedly, and with possibility it cannot oppose the explicit texts that have come. And Imam Abu Hanifa narrated with his chain that he used to recite in the first: 'Glorify the name of your Lord, the Most High' (Surah al-A'la), in the second: 'Say, O disbelievers' (Surah al-Kafirun), and in the third: 'Say, He is Allah, the One' (Surah al-Ikhlas). And what occurs in the Sunan and other works of adding the mu'awwidhatayn (Surah al-Falaq and al-Nas) was rejected by Imam Ahmad and Ibn Ma'in, and most scholars did not choose it, as mentioned by al-Tirmidhi. This is in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the number of rak'ahs and the recitation in witr. It begins by establishing that witr consists of three rak'ahs with a single taslim (salutation) at the end, citing a hadith from Aisha (ra) narrated by al-Hakim. It then addresses an objection: Ibn Umar is reported to have performed two rak'ahs separately. The response, from Hasan al-Basri, is that Umar (ra) also did that, but he would stand up for the second rak'ah with takbir (i.e., without a separate taslim), implying that the three rak'ahs are still connected. The passage then refutes the argument that the hadith 'Night prayer is two by two, and if one fears dawn, pray one to make it witr' proves that witr is a single rak'ah with a fresh intention, by noting that this hadith is ambiguous and cannot override the explicit texts. The passage then provides the specific recitation for each rak'ah as transmitted by Imam Abu Hanifa: Surah al-A'la, Surah al-Kafirun, and Surah al-Ikhlas. It notes that adding the Mu'awwidhatayn (Surah al-Falaq and al-Nas) is not authenticated by leading hadith scholars like Ahmad and Ibn Ma'in, and most scholars do not choose it. This establishes the Hanafi practice of three rak'ahs with specific surahs.

Key Terms
التسليمة (al-taslimah): The final salutation ending the prayer, saying 'Assalamu alaikum wa rahmatullah' to the right and left.
المعوذتين (al-mu'awwidhatayn): The two chapters seeking refuge: Surah al-Falaq (113) and Surah al-Nas (114).
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after the night prayer, considered wajib in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the correct recitation in the third rak'ah of witr?
A) Surah al-Fatiha only.
B) Surah al-Ikhlas.
C) Surah al-Falaq and al-Nas.
D) Surah al-A'la.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school mandates three continuous rak'ahs for witr with one taslim at the end and specific surahs for each rak'ah.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Hanafi Following a Non-Hanafi Imam in Witr
Disputes the validity of a Hanafi follower behind a Shafi'i imam in witr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on following an imam who makes taslim after two rak'ahs in witr and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between al-Zayla'i and Abu Bakr al-Razi.

Core Idea
A Hanafi follower's witr is invalid behind an imam who prays witr with two taslims.

Praying witr behind an imam from another madhhab can raise questions about validity. This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a specific scenario: a Hanafi follower behind a Shafi'i imam who prays witr as two rak'ahs with taslim, then one separate. The Hanafi school holds witr as wajib and performed as three rak'ahs with one taslim. The dispute centers on whether the follower's intention aligns with the imam's action.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position on witr
For Hanafis, witr is wajib and consists of three rak'ahs with one taslim at the end. The follower must intend this specific prayer.
2
State the issue
The imam (likely Shafi'i) prays two rak'ahs with taslim, then one rak'ah separately. Can a Hanafi follow him?
3
Follow al-Zayla'i's ruling
Al-Zayla'i authenticates that it is not permissible. The apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) from Abu Hanifa and the two companions supports this.
4
Examine Abu Bakr al-Razi's counter-argument
Al-Razi permits it, arguing the follower completes witr with the imam. This view is based on an interpretation that 'wajaba' in the hadith means 'established' not 'obligated', allowing qada.
5
Understand the tarjih (relied-upon position)
The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq notes that al-Razi's view departs from the apparent meaning. The mufta bihi is that it is not permissible, as stated by al-Zayla'i and the majority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصحح الشارح الزيلعي أنه لا يجوز اقتداء الخنفي بمن يسلم من الركعتين في الوتر وجوزه أبو بكر الرازي ويصلي معه بقية الوتر لأن الأصحاب على ظاهر الرواية عنهم ونقل جواباً آخر أن المراد إجماع الصحابة لقول الطحاوي أن وجوبه ثبت بإجماعهم وإلى هذا يشير قول الفتح أن وجب بمعنى ثبت قال : وهذا الجواب اختاره كثير الشارحين ولا يخفى أن فيه عدولاً عن الظاهر ا هـ. وفي شرح الشيخ اسمعيل والتحقيق ما في الفتح لما يلزم على ما ذكره في البحر من تفريق الأحكام ولهذا قال في المحيط. وما ذكر الجواب في ظاهر الرواية ظاهر على مذهب أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى .
And al-Zayla'i the commentator authenticated that it is not permissible for a Hanafi to follow someone who makes taslim after two rak'ahs in witr. Abu Bakr al-Razi permitted it, and he prays with him the remainder of witr, because the companions (the two companions?) are on the apparent narration from them. And he transmitted another answer that the intent is the consensus of the Companions, due to al-Tahawi's statement that its obligation is established by their consensus. And to this points the statement of al-Fath that 'wajaba' means 'thabata' (established). He said: And this is the answer chosen by many commentators. It is not hidden that in it there is a departure from the apparent. End. And in the commentary of Shaykh Isma'il and al-Tahqiq is what is in al-Fath, due to what follows from what was mentioned in al-Bahr of distinguishing rulings. For this, it was said in al-Muhit. And what was mentioned as an answer in the apparent narration is apparent on the madhhab of Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding a Hanafi follower behind an imam (likely Shafi'i) who prays witr by performing two rak'ahs with taslim and then one separately. The commentator al-Zayla'i affirms that it is not permissible for a Hanafi to follow such an imam. However, Abu Bakr al-Razi (a Hanafi scholar) permits it, arguing that the follower would pray the remaining part of witr with the imam. This is based on the 'apparent narration' (zahir al-riwaya) from the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), who might have a more lenient view. Another answer is transmitted: that the obligation of witr is established by the consensus of the Companions, and the word 'wajaba' in the hadith means 'thabata' (established) rather than 'obligated', implying that qada is required but not necessarily that witr is wajib. This answer is chosen by many commentators. However, the author of al-Bahr al-Raiq (the text we are studying) points out that this interpretation departs from the apparent meaning. The passage concludes that the answer according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) is clear on the madhhab of Abu Hanifa (that it is not permissible to follow such an imam). The dispute hinges on whether the Hanafi follower's prayer is valid if he follows an imam who prays witr in a way that differs from the Hanafi method. The relied-upon position is that it is not valid because the follower must intend the same prayer as the imam, and the imam's performance (with two taslims) breaks the unity of the prayer.

Key Terms
الاقتداء (al-iqtida): Following an imam in congregational prayer.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): The explicit narrations from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani in the six major works.
ثبوت الوجوب (thubut al-wujub): The establishment of obligation; the interpretation that 'wajaba' means 'thabata' (established).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, can a Hanafi pray behind an imam who makes taslim after two rak'ahs in witr?
A) Yes, because witr is not a fard.
B) No, it is not permissible.
C) Yes, but only if the follower prays the third rak'ah alone.
D) Yes, according to all scholars.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi may not follow an imam who breaks witr into two separate prayers with two taslims, as this violates the unity of intention required for valid iqtida.
